Fierce Battle in Northern Spain: Government Forces in Peril; Rebel Army Launches Intense Land and Air Assault on Irún; Mount Txuriarte Ridge Captured

Biarritz – Spanish government forces and rebel forces on the Irún front had temporarily ceased fighting to consolidate positions and repair defenses. However, this afternoon, the battle resumed fiercely. Both sides used machine guns and heavy artillery to bombard each other's positions. The situation for the government forces has suddenly deteriorated, with rebel forces almost entirely occupying Mount Txuriarte. The main line of defense outside Irún has been lost. Observers at the border believe the government forces are in extreme danger, as the rebels' occupation of the Txuriarte ridge allows them to control the main road from Irún to San Sebastián. (Reuters, 2nd)

Hendaye, Southern France – At dawn today, 1,500 rebel troops from the northern front, mostly Moroccan foreign legionnaires, launched another attack on Irún. Government troops bravely resisted. Heavy artillery and tanks participated in the land battle, while aircraft provided air support. The fierce battle lasted all day, resulting in a stalemate. It was one of the most intense battles since the outbreak of the Spanish Civil War. At noon, rebel aircraft dropped six large bombs on Irún, destroying the railway, station, and arsenal. The Convent of the Sacred Heart (now used as a military camp) also suffered significant damage. The explosions were so powerful that the ground even shook here in Hendaye. The rebel forces have now occupied several high points on Mount Txuriarte outside Irún and immediately installed artillery positions to bombard the city from above. In the afternoon, the rebels dispatched five armored vehicles along the main road outside Irún, opening fire on the Labanche heights, where government troops were positioned at noon. One government armored vehicle returned fire, destroying one of the rebel armored vehicles. At four o'clock in the afternoon, three government aircraft flew to the rebel positions and dropped several bombs. The rebels immediately opened fire with anti-aircraft guns, driving them away and sending one aircraft in pursuit. The two aircraft engaged in aerial combat, exchanging machine-gun fire, but neither hit. The day's fighting resulted in no change in the positions of the two armies. The wounded government troops in Irún have been transported by several ambulances to the nearby port of San Sebastián for treatment. There was no fighting in the area around that port today. (Havas, 1st)

Hendaye – Spanish government and rebel forces today resumed engaging each other with modern weaponry in the fight for the key city of Irún in northeastern Spain. Although the rebel artillery and occupied positions are superior to those of the government forces, the battle ended with no actual movement of the front lines. Government forces were forced to retreat from the banks of the Bidasoa River due to heavy artillery bombardment, and their position in San Marcial was also under constant bombardment. However, the troops loyal to the government held their main trenches and did not yield. When the fighting ceased at dusk, they still held their positions. During the engagement, artillery fire shook the heavens and the earth, and the rebel artillery fire seemed to be very accurate, so it is expected that the number of defenders killed will be very high. In the area holding the three-hundred-yard-long ridge overlooking Irún, no fewer than six hundred shells have fallen.

According to unofficial estimates, today's battle resulted in 1,600 dead and wounded. The heavy artillery bombardment on both sides caused extensive property damage. It is reported that no fewer than twenty-seven buildings were destroyed. The most severely damaged was the Jesus School, which is located near the railway station and is currently used as the headquarters of the labor union. The area along the Spanish-French border was also devastated by artillery fire. Shells, bombs, and bullets rained down all day near the French border. The red-roofed Spanish farmhouses between Arrantzale and Abentza are riddled with bullet holes. When the fighting stopped, many farmhouses were still billowing smoke.

General Mola, commander of the rebel forces in the north, personally visited the front lines today to supervise the battle. The most critical moment of the battle occurred shortly after noon when rebel armored vehicles drove to within a hundred yards of the government barracks, less than a mile from Behobia. The rebels launched repeated assaults but were repulsed by government machine-gun fire. The rebels eventually abandoned dozens of dead and wounded on the battlefield and retreated to their defensive positions. The government forces then deployed renowned bomb throwers, daring miners who fearlessly charged forward, using poorly made bombs and hand grenades. They bravely threw the grenades and explosives into the rebel ranks. Even veteran foreign legion soldiers were overwhelmed. When the artillery fire finally subsided, the government forces had expended a great deal of ammunition but achieved nothing.

Government pursuit planes and rebel bombers engaged in aerial combat several times during the day, and anti-aircraft guns fired frequently. The ambulance crews were extremely busy all day, making frequent trips up and down the hills around Irún, carrying wounded soldiers from the front lines to the aid stations as the battle raged. (Reuters, 1st)

On-the-Ground Inspection of the Irún Front

Hendaye – An inspection of the Irún front reveals that the rebels' heavy bombardment of government positions yesterday achieved nothing. The rebels have not dug new trenches, while government reinforcements are hiding in the craters left by the destroyed bunkers on the foothills. Rifle and machine-gun fire continued throughout the night, apparently to cover the noise of the armored vehicles transporting ammunition to the front lines. (Reuters, 2nd)

Heavy Artillery Fire Shakes the Border with France; Government Troops Hold Firm in Trenches; Grenade Squads Show Remarkable Bravery

Billière, Southern France – Today, heavy fighting occurred between government and rebel forces in northern Spain near the French border. Shells rained down on Billière (in Spanish territory) across the Bidasoa River, completely destroying the trenches. Many Spanish farmhouses with red tile roofs, renowned for scenic beauty, between Arrantzale and Labanche, were struck and burned. The fires are still burning. A portion of the nearby fir forest was also destroyed. This evening, rebel artillery began a heavy bombardment of government trenches. Through binoculars, it was evident the government forces sustained significant damage, but soldiers in the trenches remained steadfast, holding their original positions. They launched counterattacks with grenade squads, throwing grenades and explosives at the rebels, causing heavy casualties and forcing a slight retreat. At 6:00 PM, the rebel artillery, aided by the Fort Guadalupe battery, heavily bombarded Irún, hitting trenches and creating huge craters, with earth flying everywhere. However, the government forces fought bravely, and the trenches did not budge. The government artillery at Fuenterrabía returned fire, with two shells landing near the rebels' second line of defense on the mountainside. At 7:00 PM, the fighting was still ongoing. (Havas, 1st)

Lisbon – General Mola, commander of the rebel forces in northern Spain, told visitors today that the day of the revolution's victory is approaching, but the war will likely last until the end of winter. He does not believe that the countries can maintain neutrality and criticized the French Popular Front for openly assisting the Spanish Marxists. (Reuters, 2nd)

Official War Report: Victory After Victory on the Front Lines; Rebel Aircraft Continue to Bomb Madrid

Madrid – Government forces in the north have intensified their pressure on the rebel forces in Huesca and have completely encircled the city, cutting off all communication. In the southwestern province of Extremadura, government forces are also achieving victory after victory. Regarding the Irún front in the north, although the rebel forces have attacked for seven consecutive days, they have not succeeded. All key strategic locations around the city, such as the Labanche plateau, remain under government control. Yesterday, the 50-member grenade squad was the most effective government unit. These soldiers are highly skilled and accurate in throwing grenades, causing repeated damage to the rebel positions and greatly shaking the rebel forces. Therefore, the grenade squad deserves the greatest credit. (Havas, 2nd)

Madrid – An aircraft listening post reported this morning that several rebel aircraft were flying toward the capital, intending to bomb it. The sirens were immediately sounded to warn the public to take shelter in cellars. At the same time, anti-aircraft guns opened fire on the rebel aircraft. The rebel aircraft were unsuccessful and returned to their base. After half an hour, the situation in the capital returned to normal. (Havas, 1st)

Lisbon – The rebel radio station in Cádiz reported today that the rebel forces killed 300 people when they bombed the Ministry of War, the Ministry of the Interior, and the post office in Madrid on Friday night and Saturday morning. Meanwhile, the rebel radio station in Burgos claimed that rebel aircraft also bombed Navalperal, burning down the gasoline storage depot there. The number of casualties is unknown. However, the government radio station claimed that government aircraft dropped four bombs on Ávila, killing four people. (Guomin, 1st)

Spanish Morocco: Indigenous People Showing Signs of Unrest; Dissatisfied with the Rebel Government; Refusing to Enlist

Casablanca – Reliable sources here reported today that the indigenous people of Spanish Morocco are nearing open revolt against the rebel leaders' uprising. Although the military commander of the rebel forces has implemented repressive measures to suppress the unrest, it has only made the people more hostile to the rebel forces. It is claimed that the government has also sent people to lure the indigenous people with money and weapons, inciting them to revolt. It is reported that the indigenous people have stopped voluntarily enlisting in the rebel forces, even though the pay and food are better than their usual living standards. Today, indigenous leaders even visited Tetouan to protest the harsh policies of the rebel leaders and demanded the release of Touress, the Muslim leader currently detained in Ceuta. At the same time, 1,500 Arab women gathered at the rebel headquarters in Tetouan, demanding news of their husbands and requesting the food and money that had been promised. (Guomin, 1st)

Tangier, International Neutral Zone – Yesterday, reports emerged that the indigenous people of Spanish Morocco were increasingly dissatisfied with the rebel forces and refused to enlist, a situation that seemed quite serious. However, according to inquiries made by our reporter, order within the region is well maintained. However, the indigenous soldiers have occasionally expressed dissatisfaction because their pay is not delivered monthly. There are also Arab Muslims inciting the indigenous people not to cooperate with the rebel forces. As a result, the enlistment of indigenous people has virtually stopped. In addition, the Spanish Moroccan authorities have been treating people entering Spanish Morocco from Tangier and French Morocco quite harshly. The International Administration Committee of this port has therefore decided that all those arriving in this port from Spanish Morocco must present a passport. If the Spanish Moroccan authorities do not change their attitude, the International Committee plans to ban the export of automobiles to the region as a form of protest. (Havas, 3rd)

Málaga Coast – British and German Warships Bombed; Preparing to File Strong Protests with the Rebel Forces

Gibraltar – An accident occurred today near the Spanish port of Málaga, located sixty-five miles northeast of Gibraltar, involving the Spanish rebel forces and the navies of Great Britain and Germany. A rebel aircraft dropped four bombs on the British cruiser HMS "Wasps" and a German destroyer. Fortunately, all four bombs landed in the nearby water and did not hit. The incident was likely due to the aircraft mistaking the warships for Spanish government vessels. However, Great Britain and Germany are expected to file strong protests with the rebel headquarters in Burgos. It is said that this is the second time in recent days that foreign ships have been attacked by Spanish aircraft. The US destroyer "Kane" was bombed by a plane of unknown origin last Sunday, but was also not hit. (Reuters, 2nd)

Spain: Cabinet Expands; Inviting Left-Wing Parties to Join the New Cabinet; Hoping for Effective Assistance from France

Madrid – Former Socialist Party cabinet member Prieto told a reporter from Havas, "Prime Minister Quiroga is currently conducting negotiations to change and expand the current cabinet organization so that figures from parties of the Popular Front that have not yet joined the government, such as the Socialist Party, the Communist Party, and the Basque Nationalist Party, can also join the cabinet." Referring to international issues, Prieto said, "I do not want to be critical of France's attitude towards us. However, if France were to go a little further than its current attitude and support the Spanish government, that is something France can and should do. Because other countries are providing assistance to the rebel forces, even if France has some reservations, it could still provide us with effective assistance." (Havas, 1st)

Week of Prayers for World Peace in Churches Across Britain

(London) The Archbishop of Canterbury has called on all churches across the country to hold special prayers on September 13th and 20th, asking for God's blessing so that the General Assembly and the Administrative Council of the League of Nations will achieve results when they meet on those two days to consider issues of world peace. (Reuters, 1st)

Spanish Rebel Leader Promises Germany Territory in Exchange for Support: Reported by French Newspaper Reporter

(Paris) Mrs. Tabouis, a diplomatic correspondent for the newspaper "L'Œuvre," recently stated that General Franco, leader of the rebel forces in southern Spain, had promised German leader Adolf Hitler that, once successful, he would cede the territory of Spanish Rio de Oro in Africa to Germany as a reward. Franco has also accepted the advice of the German Ministry of Foreign Affairs and made promises to Arab leaders in Spanish Morocco that, once victorious, he would grant the ten groups broad autonomy. They have now been permitted to publish a nationalist newspaper, "The Riff Tribune." (Havas, 2nd)

British Cabinet Holds Meeting; Discussing Three Current Issues; Baldwin and Eden Absent

(London) At their second meeting after the vacation, cabinet members today discussed the overall situation in Spain and paid attention to the progress of the non-intervention plan. The meeting also considered the attitude Britain should take towards League of Nations reform when the League of Nations meets in Geneva at the end of this month. The situation in Palestine was also touched upon. Prime Minister Baldwin was still out of the capital, so the meeting was chaired by Home Secretary Simon. (Reuters, 2nd)

(London) Foreign Secretary Eden has been feeling unwell recently. The Foreign Office issued a statement saying, "The Foreign Secretary has a slight fever and the doctor has ordered him to rest in bed for a few days." (Reuters, 2nd)

Issue of the Non-Intervention Agreement: Britain Urges Germany and Portugal to Cooperate; Requesting Joining the International Coordinating Committee

(London) France has proposed that a consultative committee be formed by representatives of the major powers participating in the non-intervention agreement on the Spanish Civil War. The British government also believes this is essential because without such a body, there would be no proper way to discuss the points of contention arising from the agreement. The British government also wants this committee to meet in London next week. France has asked Germany to join, and the British Chargé d'Affaires in Berlin, Newton, has also been instructed to assist France in urging the German government to cooperate with this initiative as soon as possible. Sir Wingfield, the British Ambassador to Lisbon, is also in contact with the Portuguese government on this matter. (Reuters, 1st)

(London) The Foreign Office is rushing to convene an international committee to monitor the non-intervention policy of European powers in the Spanish Civil War. Officials here are very concerned about Portugal's active support for the rebel forces, despite its statements otherwise. There are also reports that German aircraft and personnel are serving the rebel forces. Therefore, it is believed here that the process of non-intervention policy must be completed quickly to avoid serious involvement of various countries in the Spanish political situation. (Guomin, 1st)

(Berlin) The Portuguese Legation in Germany published a statement in the "Berliner Tageblatt" here regarding the adoption of a neutral policy on the Spanish Civil War, stating, "Although the Portuguese government generally accepts the notes from the British and French governments regarding the ban on arms, this acceptance is actually subject to certain reservations. Now, foreign newspapers only point out that the Portuguese government has accepted the proposals of Britain and France, implying that this acceptance is not subject to reservations, or that even if there are reservations, they are not important to the Portuguese government and the governments participating in the arms embargo agreement. This is truly regrettable." The most important reservations put forward by the Portuguese government are two: (1) The Soviet Union must accept the non-intervention agreement at the same time as all relevant countries; (2) Portugal's security must be guaranteed. (Havas, 1st)

Romania and Russia/Poland; Maintaining Existing Friendship; Exchanging Diplomatic Messages; Former Romanian Foreign Minister Recuperating in France

(Moscow) The Soviet newspapers all published the texts of the telegrams exchanged between Litvinov and the new Romanian Foreign Minister Antonescu, as follows:

Antonescu's telegram read, "As I assume my new position, I deeply wish to express to Your Excellency my sincere belief in the possibility of cooperating with you to maintain peace and further deepen the friendly relations that have always existed between our two countries. I hope that I will receive Your Excellency's valuable assistance so that I can complete my new task."

Litvinov's reply read, "I am very pleased to learn of Your Excellency's hope to cooperate with me to jointly maintain peace and deepen the friendly relations between our two countries. I particularly welcome Your Excellency's wishes, as cooperation with all countries, especially neighboring countries, to consolidate world peace is the basic policy of the Soviet Union, and such cooperation is especially needed in the current international situation." (Reuters, 1st)

Warsaw – The new Romanian Foreign Minister, Antonescu, sent a telegram to Polish Foreign Minister Colonel Beck, saying that Romania and Poland are allied nations with a cordial relationship. He is happy to cooperate with Beck to "promote the existing relationship between the two countries and jointly maintain peace," now that he has taken office as Romanian Foreign Minister. Colonel Beck replied with a similar telegram of thanks. (Havas, 1st)

Monte Carlo – Former Romanian Foreign Minister Titulescu, now recuperating near Nice in southern France, has seen his health improve and will soon return to his country. It is rumored that the Romanian government has asked him to serve as its representative to the League of Nations, but those close to Titulescu have denied this. (Havas, 1st)

French Army Autumn Exercises; Polish Army Chief Inspector Visits

Reims, France – Polish Army Chief Inspector General Rydz-Śmigły, accompanied by General Gamellin, Chief of Staff, visited the Champagne and Verdun areas yesterday to commemorate the battlefields of the European War and to observe the French Army's autumn exercises. He returned to this city for rest that evening. This morning at 6:30, he once again accompanied General Gamellin to the Suippes area to continue observing the large-scale exercises of the 2nd and 14th Divisions of the Army. President Lebrun is also scheduled to arrive in the city at 10:00 this morning, where he will meet with General Rydz-Śmigły and personally award him a first-class honor. (Havas, 2nd)

British First Lord of the Admiralty Visits Haifa Harbour on Warship

(London) According to reports from Malta, British First Lord of the Admiralty Sir Samuel Hoare has sailed to Haifa to inspect the British warships and naval forces stationed there. (Reuters, 1st)

Naval Issues: Japanese Reply to Britain; Requesting Increased Submarine Tonnage

(London) The British government informed the Japanese and US governments on July 15th of this year that it intends to invoke the escalator clause of the 1930 London Naval Treaty to maintain the total tonnage of destroyers at 190,000 tons (the London Naval Treaty stipulated 150,000 tons) due to the additional naval power reserved by other countries. Japanese Ambassador Shigeru Yoshida delivered his government's reply to the British government this morning, stating that after the British government increased the total tonnage of destroyers stipulated in the London Naval Treaty by 40,000 tons, Japan could originally increase the total tonnage of destroyers by 28,000 tons according to the ratio. However, it only wants to increase it by 11,590 tons, and increase the submarine tonnage by 15,598 tons, totaling 27,188 tons, to compensate. Officials in the British government declined to comment on Japan's reply. Political figures believe that although Japan has requested an increase in the total tonnage of submarines, the British government will not invoke the escalator clause again and propose an increase in the total tonnage of submarines. They said that although Japan's action is not legal, it is still honest and forthright. (Havas, 2nd)

Britain Issues New Stamps: 30 Million Stamps Sold in One Day

(London) The new stamps of King Edward VIII were issued for the first time today. Purchases across the country were exceptionally enthusiastic. Post offices across the nation opened from early in the morning until late at night, and the throngs of buyers never ceased. Employees in the bureaus were overwhelmed. It is estimated that 30 million stamps were sold. The daily average number of stamps sold is usually just 20 million. Only 300 million of this batch of stamps has been released and these will only be sufficient for a week or ten days. After they are sold out, continued distribution will wait for the currently stored stamps of the late King George to be sold. (Reuters, 1st)

Lloyd George to Visit Hitler in Germany: Discussing the International Situation

(London) Lloyd George will depart for Germany today with his son and one of his daughters to hold informal talks with German leader Hitler on the situation in Europe and the world. He also plans to inspect German agricultural plans and labor camps in Gotha. (Reuters, 1st)

Molotov Resumes Duties After Rumored Dismissal

(Moscow) Mr. Molotov of the Soviet Union resumed his duties on August 31st, having ended his leave. (Havas, 2nd)

Stalin Ill? Bizarre Reports from French Newspapers

(Paris) "Le Matin" received a report from its Moscow correspondent stating that it is widely rumored that Stalin is seriously ill. Stalin suffered from liver disease in 1926, which prevented him from engaging in politics for three years. The fact that Stalin did not attend the performance of the Zorkina Art Troupe in Moscow has increased the credibility of this rumor, as the troupe is specially invited by Stalin every year. The correspondent also said that at the official banquet for the troupe, a toast was raised to the "absent and fatigued" Stalin. (Guomin, 2nd)

Resolving Border Disputes: Manchukuo and Mongolia Reopen Negotiations at the End of This Month in Manchouli

(Moscow) Regarding the imminent reopening of the "Manchu-Mongol Conference," a TASS correspondent stationed in Ulan Bator (Kulun) has obtained reliable information from the Mongolian side. It is said that since the meeting of Mongol and "Manchu" representatives held at Manchouli Station in 1935, which broke down at the end of November due to the excessive demands of the Manchukuo representatives, it is well known that border conflicts occurred frequently in the area of Buir Lake in December, January, and February. As a result, the border situation in "Manchukuo" has become unusually tense. Based on its consistent sincerity in peacefully resolving border disputes, the government of the Mongolian People's Republic sent a telegram to the "Manchu" government on February 29 of this year, suggesting the immediate formation of a committee to investigate the situation and causes of the border conflicts. However, the "Manchukuo" government's reply to the above suggestion put forward many demands that the Mongolian government could not accept, and stated that acceptance of these demands was a prerequisite for reopening negotiations. However, in subsequent telegraphic negotiations, the "Manchu" side abandoned its proposed preconditions. As a result of the exchange of letters between the two sides, they both agreed to reopen the conference at Manchouli Station on September 25 of this year to discuss the establishment of two joint Mongol-Manchu committees, one dedicated to investigating the existing border between Mongolia and Manchukuo, and the other dedicated to investigating the circumstances and causes of past conflicts, in order to resolve border incidents. In addition to the second committee, both sides should also dispatch several permanent official representatives to resolve all border disputes and determine the areas where these representatives will be stationed. (TASS Dispatch, 1st)

Aviation Competition Held Between London and South Africa; Fourteen Entrants Already; Departing from Portsmouth on the 29th of This Month

(London) According to an announcement made today by the Racing Committee of the Royal Aero Club in London, fourteen well-known British racing pilots have currently joined the Schlesinger Air Race from London to Johannesburg, which will depart from Portsmouth on September 29. The participating aircraft will take off every minute starting from 6:15 in the morning. These time differences will be corrected upon arrival in Cairo, as that is the only official control point for this race. In addition, all racing pilots must change direction at the Simun airfield in Belgrade, the capital of Yugoslavia, and someone must be able to confirm this. It is said that Imperial Airways has agreed to be responsible for the management of lights and all ground affairs at major airfields along the route from Cairo to Johannesburg. From September 29 to October 1, the lights at each airfield will be illuminated all night without being extinguished. Of the fourteen people who have registered, three are from South Africa and one is from India. As for the aircraft participating in the competition, there are three Miles aircraft, four Vegas aircraft, three Manners aircraft, two Hawk aircraft, and one De Havilland and Envoys aircraft each. Well-known pilots who have joined include Mr. Smith, Mr. Rose, and Mr. Scott. (Reuters Dispatch, 2nd)

Completion of the Northeast Meiping Railway Line; Operations to Commence Within Days

(Changchun) The Meiping Railway Line, built by the puppet Railway Bureau from Sipingjie to Meihekou, was completed at the end of last month and will begin operations within days. (Hualianshe Dispatch, 2nd)

Soviet Russia Reduces Military Service Age; 600,000 Young People Conscripted; Army Exceeds 1.3 Million; France Considers Extending Military Service Length

(Moscow) Six hundred thousand young people born in 1914-1915 were conscripted today. It is said that although this step will temporarily cause the Soviet army to greatly exceed its usual strength of 1.3 million soldiers, the size of the Soviet army will return to its normal state after the oldest age groups are finally discharged. This Soviet conscription of all those born in 1914 and half of those born in 1915 has brought into effect the recent order reducing the age of military service to nineteen. (Reuters Dispatch, 2nd)

(Paris) The right-wing *Figaro* recently reported that after Germany lengthened the term of compulsory military service, the French government intends to extend the term of military service (currently two years) as a countermeasure. Defense Minister Daladier met with President Lebrun, Senate Army Committee Chairman Vansant, and House Army Committee Chairman La Chambre yesterday to discuss this matter, and the meeting lasted a long time. The Council of Ministers will also discuss this matter at its meeting on Friday, September 4. The newspaper also said that Daladier and Vansant both advocated increasing the term of military service to two and a half years, which La Chambre and left-wing figures still consider insufficient. The government's decision on this matter will likely be based on the opinion of the High Committee of National Defense. (Havas Dispatch, 2nd)

(Paris) After the newspaper *Figaro* issued a report stating that the German government intended to lengthen the term of compulsory military service and the French government also intended to take similar measures to counter it, those in charge recently announced that the cabinet is scheduled to hold a cabinet meeting at the Prime Minister's Office at 4:00 PM on the 7th of this month, at which time Defense Minister Daladier will propose various measures to deal with Germany. (Havas Agency Dispatch, 2nd)

(Paris) Qidong (Communist Party member), the vice chairman of the House Army Committee, recently sent a letter to La Chambre, the chairman of the committee, requesting the immediate convening of the committee to discuss the issue of extending the term of military service. La Chambre replied that this matter would be determined by the cabinet's opinion, and that the Army Committee could be convened after the Council of Ministers and the military authorities in charge had thoroughly studied it. According to legal regulations, the term of military service in the French army was originally only one year, but due to the reduced birth rate during the European War, the number of new recruits from 1935 to May 1940 was greatly insufficient, so the term of military service was increased to two years to remedy the situation. (Havas Dispatch, 2nd)

Russia and Spain Celebrate International Youth Day; Large-Scale Parades and Demonstrations Held; Slogans Shouting Against Fascism

(London) Yesterday, large-scale parades and demonstrations were held in both Madrid and Moscow to celebrate International Youth Day. In Madrid, more than 100,000 people, including militiamen, members of the People's Front, and various children's groups, paraded through the streets, claiming that their parades and demonstrations were a countermeasure against the ineffective air raids by the rebel forces. The celebration ceremony in Moscow was even larger in scale, with about 500,000 young men and women, including the recently conscripted soldiers, all parading inside Red Square, where they were inspected by Chairman Molotov of the People's Committee and Defense Commissioner Voroshilov. Despite the cold weather and incessant rain, the men and women in this parade still marched through the city for several hours, singing and dancing along the way, and shouting "Down with Fascism." Each marcher held wooden signs, flags, and satirical drawings, most of which were against Hitler and Fascism, and expressed disapproval of the Spanish government. One student held a wooden sign with the words "The world today is on the eve of Fascist Germany and militarist Japan carrying out wars to conquer others." (Reuters Dispatch, 2nd)

(Moscow) Yesterday was the 22nd International Youth Day. The Moscow Youth Association held a grand demonstration parade. Thousands of Moscow youth held flags and wore flowers, sang and played music, and marched in formation in Red Square, passing the Lenin Mausoleum and the platform, demonstrating the power and spirit of youth. On the platform were Motov, Kaganovich, Voroshilov, Ordzhonikidze, Andreyev, Gyumar, Khrushchev, Budyonny, Secretary Lukyanov of the Central Committee of the All-Union League of Young Communists, and other party and state leaders. After the youth parade, there was a parade of armed members of the Communist Youth League. In addition to Moscow, youth in other cities and towns in the Soviet Union also held grand commemorative activities. (TASS Dispatch, 2nd)

Explanation from German Nationals in Shanghai Regarding Germany's Extension of Military Service

National News Agency Report: Our agency's reporter noted that Germany's recent extension of the term of military service from one year to three years has caused considerable surprise internationally, with many fearing that a new major war will arise as a result. However, the actual situation is quite different. It is undeniable that the countries of Europe are at odds. If one wishes to maintain peace in this situation, the only way to do so is to ensure that the strength of each country is equal. Recently, Soviet Russia advanced the conscription age to nineteen, a move that would allow the Red Army to increase by two million men in peacetime. In addition, the term of military service in countries such as Soviet Russia, France, Czechoslovakia, Poland, and Japan is two years, and Italy's is eighteen months. In March of this year, France changed its term of military service to two years, citing the reasons that there were not many children born during the European War and that the number of soldiers was lacking, as well as military training. Why should this be any different for Germany? Because soldiers in the new era must have the ability to act independently and must have technical knowledge. A one-year term of military service is difficult to provide sufficient training. However, even under these circumstances, Germany initially still implemented a one-year term of military service in the hope that other countries would follow suit. Later, in view of the fact that neighboring countries not only still adhered to the two-year military service system, but also, among them, especially Soviet Russia, continued to expand without end, it had no choice but to change the term of military service to two years to compare with other countries, with no other intention. Germany's move is not only for its own security, but also for the security of Europe. In short, the German people and their government desire peace as much as other countries, but in view of the fact that the military preparations of other countries are a major threat to Germany's security and world peace, it has no choice but to take this step to adapt to its environment. The above are the opinions of German nationals in Shanghai that our reporter interviewed.

(London) The Egyptian delegation, which came here last week to sign the new Anglo-Egyptian treaty, departed from Victoria Station this morning to return to their country. Nahas also expressed, on behalf of the delegation, the great enthusiasm with which the British government and people welcomed them. (Reuters Dispatch, 1st)

Orders

The National Government issued an order on the 2nd stating that the Provisional Income Tax Regulations will be implemented from October 1, 1936. The income from salaries and remuneration of public servants in the second category of the regulations, and the income from interest on public bonds and deposits in the third category, will be collected starting from October 1, 1936. All other items will be collected starting from January 1, 1937. This order also ordered that Yu Hanmou concurrently serve as a member of the Central Military Academy's Academic Affairs Committee. This order also ordered that Wang Zigang be appointed as the employer representative of the Republic of China at the 21st and 22nd Maritime Conferences of the International Labor Bureau. This order also ordered that Chiang Tingfu, the Director of the Political Affairs Department of the Executive Yuan, be assigned to another position, and Chiang Tingfu should be relieved of his current position. This order appointed Liang Long as the Envoy Extraordinary and Minister Plenipotentiary of the Republic of China to the Czechoslovak Republic. International Commercial Telegrams, September 2, Special Commercial Report from Reuters

Gold and Silver

The London gold price today was 138 shillings and 3 pence, up half a penny.

London silver was stable today, with prices unchanged. Spot and futures prices were still 19 pence 6875. India bought and then sold. Buyers were satisfied.

Montreal silver fell slightly this morning. The December futures price fell 10 pounds at the opening to 44.70-44.95.

Exchange Rates

The British-American London foreign exchange market was only stable today, with not much activity. The British-American exchange rate opened at 9 yuan 031875, which was 15625 lower than the American-British closing price yesterday. It rose 125 within an hour to 5 yuan 033125. This price was unchanged at 1:00 PM.

Securities

The New York stock market opened quite stable this morning. Then, as the market was flooded with buy orders, most stock prices rose, as good earnings reports were released. The situation for steel, railway, and automobile stocks was all excellent. Steel and railways each rose by about one yuan. Trading was lively near noon. Buying interest in major stocks was strong. Utility stocks and copper stocks also had considerable trading, but oil stocks still lagged behind. The New York stock market prices are listed below:

Cotton and Wheat

The New York cotton market was stable today due to good Liverpool news. Later, due to favorable buying sentiment and short covering, prices continued to rise. Farmers are now taking a wait-and-see attitude, waiting for the release of the Department of Agriculture's report, and because the weather is expected to be mild. At 11:00, the December futures price was 11.58, which was 11 points higher than yesterday's closing price.

The Liverpool cotton market was stable today. At 1:00 PM, the October futures price rose 9 points to 6.27.

Chicago wheat was quiet and uneventful today. Prices fluctuated very little, and trading was scarce. Before noon, the December futures price was 107.50, up 375. The feed market situation was quiet and dull.

Liverpool wheat opened steady. Sellers were unwilling to release supplies because they saw a lack of excitement, so they kept them in reserve. The market situation then became looser. At 1:00 PM, the October futures price was 7 shillings 1 penny 375, which was 625 lower than yesterday's closing price.

Rubber

The London rubber market situation was stable today. The transaction price was 7 pence 5, the same as yesterday's final price.

Resolutions of the Central Political Council on National Elections: Compliance with Laws and Regulations Required, Excessive Hospitality and Entertainment Prohibited to Maintain Integrity; Appointment of Li Denghui, Feng Ziyou, et al. as Legislative Members

(Nanjing) The Central Political Council held its twentieth meeting on the morning of the 2nd. Committee Member Sun Ke acted as chairman. The following resolutions were learned: A letter to the National Government to order all officials and people nationwide to strictly abide by laws and regulations, faithfully perform their duties, and refrain from any illegal acts in the election of National Assembly representatives. All agencies should not engage in excessive hospitality and entertainment towards electors, candidates, and representatives, except for matters to be handled in accordance with laws and regulations, in order to maintain the integrity of the election and set an example for constitutional governance. The Executive Yuan requested amendments to the Compulsory Execution Law to be submitted to the Legislative Yuan for review. The outline for organizing farmland water conservancy along the rivers and lakes was approved and submitted to the Executive Yuan for implementation. Permission was granted to the Ministry of Finance to issue 120 million yuan in public bonds to consolidate Guangdong's finances, approved in principle. The draft of the public bond regulations, etc., was submitted to the Legislative Yuan for deliberation. Permission was granted to the Control Yuan to establish an audit office in Guangdong Province. Li Denghui, Feng Ziyou, Wang Yuxiang, Lin Gengbai, and Aisha were appointed as legislative members of the Legislative Yuan. The National Government's appointments and removals of ambassadors to Russia and the United States, as well as members and directors of the Guizhou Provincial Government, were ratified. (Nanjing) The election of representatives from free professional groups in Nanjing City is scheduled to take place on the 9th at the municipal government. The groups include the Lawyers Association, the Accountants Association, the Physicians Association, and the National Physicians Association. (Special dispatch from the 2nd)

(Nanjing) The General Office of the National Election answered the questions from the Chief Supervisor of the Jiangsu Election, stating that "the heads of all levels" mentioned in Article 58 of the Election Law refer to the heads of government offices at all levels. All responsible personnel of county government affiliated agencies, such as the heads of various bureaus, district chiefs of sub-district offices, and directors of public funds and property management offices, are subject to the same restrictions. However, the directors of relief homes, county hospitals, and county opium suppression centers fall within the scope of social undertakings and should not be subject to these restrictions. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 2nd)

(Nanjing) Regarding the election affairs of military representatives, since national ID cards for all officers and soldiers cannot be universally issued, the question arises as to whether their citizenship status still exists after voting and upon retirement. The General Office of the National Election previously requested clarification and the response was: After an elector votes, the voting manager will stamp the words "Voting Completed" on the citizen's card and return the original card. Therefore, whether citizenship exists should be determined by whether or not a citizen's card is held. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 2nd)

(Nanjing) The Provincial Party Headquarters of Shandong previously telegraphed requesting clarification on whether section chiefs and others in counties where bureaus have been abolished and departments merged are subject to the restrictions of Article 58 of the detailed rules. The General Office of the National Election has replied by telegram stating that, in counties where bureaus have been abolished and departments merged, although the personnel administration and powers of the section chiefs and directors are the same as those of bureaus, there is a distinction according to the County Organization Law and the Outline of Measures for Abolishing Bureaus and Merging Departments in Anti-Banditry Provinces. They are merely assistant administrators of the county government and should not be considered "heads of government offices." Therefore, they should not be subject to the restrictions of Article 58 of the implementing rules. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 2nd)

(Nanjing) The General Office of the National Election recently answered three questions raised by the Chief Supervisor of the Hunan Election: Each county must have at least one candidate. If the number of candidates initially nominated in each county is less than the statutory number, should a second nomination be held? The law does not explicitly stipulate this, but in terms of electoral duties and rights, a second nomination may be held. However, only one supplementary nomination is allowed. The minimum number of votes required is five. If this number is not reached, a supplementary nomination is not allowed, but only one supplementary nomination should be held. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 2nd)

(Nanjing) The General Office of the National Election recently answered questions from the Chief Supervisor of the Jiangsu Election regarding the participation of industrial and commercial organizations in the election: A shop that has joined a chamber of commerce, only its representative may be regarded as a member of a member organization under Article 24, Section 2 of the Election Law. According to the precedent of the National Assembly, they are allowed to participate in the election, but they do not have the right to nominate. Others who meet the qualifications of Article 3 of the Election Law should still be regional voters. Whether members of industrial organizations can be voters in the elections of their respective professional organizations depends on whether the organization is a trade union established in accordance with the Trade Union Law. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 2nd)

(Nanjing) The General Office of the National Election previously approved a letter from the General Office of the election of representatives of free professional groups requesting clarification of ambiguities. The General Office answered them item by item. The members of a faculty organization that encompasses a university or independent college are limited to faculty members of that university or college when elected. The qualifications of members of faculty organizations are not explicitly stipulated in the Election Law and its implementing rules. Therefore, according to the Regulations on the Qualifications of University Faculty, all professors, lecturers, assistant instructors, and part-time teachers of a university or independent college should be included. However, their candidate qualifications must fully comply with the provisions of Article 21 of the Election Law. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 2nd)

(Hankou) The special district of the city has a citizen population of over 4,000, but has long lacked a self-governing organization. Therefore, in the Hankou regional election for the National Assembly representatives, the district should establish a temporary nomination district and elect three temporary fang chiefs to serve as nominators for the Hankou representatives. It was reported on the 2nd that citizens in the district used communication methods to elect Xu Weirong, Tang Lujian, and Zhou Xichen as temporary fang chiefs. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 2nd)

(Wuhu) Shao Hua, a member of the Central Committee and national election supervisor for Anhui and Jiangxi, arrived in Wuhu from Nanjing on the 2nd at noon. Commissioner Gao, Director Yu, and representatives from various organizations welcomed him at the station. In the evening, he traveled to Anqing with Miao Peicheng by ship and will soon proceed to Jiangxi. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 2nd)

(Guangzhou) Wang Yingyu, chief supervisor of the Guangdong National Assembly election, telegraphed all counties and cities on the 2nd, limiting them to holding citizen swearing-in registration within ten days and submitting voter lists for verification. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 2nd)

Rumors of the Dalai Lama's Reincarnation Unconfirmed

(Nanjing) According to a Reuters dispatch from the 1st, there are rumors that the 14th Dalai Lama has been reincarnated somewhere in Tibet. Reporters inquired with relevant parties, who all stated that they have not received such reports. Even the most recent telegrams from Tibet did not mention this matter. It is difficult to confirm this rumor without inquiring with the Tibetan side. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 1st)

(Nanjing) Cheng Yun, the former special envoy escorting the Panchen Lama into Tibet, resigned and left Qinghai last month, arriving in Nanjing on the evening of the 31st. On the 2nd, he visited Wu Zhongxin, Weng Wenhao, and Jiang Tingfu at the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission and the Executive Yuan to report on the preparations for the Panchen Lama's entry into Tibet. He then visited Zhao Shouyu, the newly appointed special envoy, urging him to go to Qinghai as soon as possible. It is learned that the Panchen Lama has left Labrang Monastery and set off for Tibet, accompanied by all his staff and entourage. According to the itinerary, he is expected to arrive at Jialasi Temple in the next day or two, stay there for a week, and continue west, arriving in Yushu County on the Tibetan border in early October. The Panchen Lama's travelling headquarters telegraphed Nanjing on the 1st, urging Zhao Shouyu to depart as soon as possible. The Panchen Lama intends to wait in Yushu to travel to Lhasa together. It takes more than a month to travel from Yushu to Lhasa. The Panchen Lama is expected to arrive in Tibet within the Gregorian calendar year. The people of both the front and rear Tibet are preparing to welcome him. A telegram was recently sent stating that the Dalai Lama has been reincarnated in a certain place. According to the Dalai Lama's office, no telegram has been received. The Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission telegraphed Tibet to inquire. One rumor is that when the Panchen Lama was in Ta'er Monastery in Qinghai, he conveyed that the Dalai Lama had been reincarnated within the territory. The truth of the matter is yet to be verified. It is understood that, according to past customs for the reincarnation of the Panchen Lama and the Dalai Lama, they are both generated through mutual prayers and must undergo proper elections. Therefore, after the passing of the 13th Dalai Lama, the reincarnation of the 14th Dalai Lama must wait for the Panchen Lama to return to Tibet, undergo prayers, and send personnel out to search before it can be determined. The rites are very complex. (Special dispatch from the 2nd)

(Nanjing) According to the Ministry of Communications, the promotion of postal services in Tibet was previously impossible due to unrest and traffic obstruction in the Kham and Tibet regions. Now that the Panchen Lama is entering Tibet, the Directorate General of Posts is sending personnel to Gansu to accompany him. After conducting on-the-ground surveys of the situation in various places, further planning will be carried out. Xikang is the throat of transportation between Tibet and the inland. In the future, it is planned to expand the postal route westward from Xikang as the first step. (Special dispatch from the 2nd)

The Legislative Yuan Reviewed Budget Proposals from Various Provinces Yesterday

(Nanjing) The Finance Committee of the Legislative Yuan held a meeting on the morning of the 2nd to review budget proposals. It approved the general local budgets for Hubei and Ningxia provinces for the 24th year of the Republic and the supplementary budget for the Hubei dyke project for the 23rd year of the Republic. These have been submitted to the full council for deliberation. In addition, the Local Autonomy Law Committee has amended the County Autonomy Law in accordance with the principles of the amended local autonomy laws promulgated by the central government and has submitted it to this week's council for deliberation. The other three cases of amending the Municipal Autonomy Law and the Implementing Law of County and Municipal Autonomy are still under review. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 2nd)

Representatives of the Tianjin Weaving and Dyeing Industry Arrived in Nanjing to Petition the Ministry

(Nanjing) The Tianjin Weaving and Dyeing Industry Association dispatched representatives Ba Lunquan, Chen Guanyu, and Chen Jieqing to Beijing on the 1st to petition the Ministry of Finance because the Tianjin Customs had investigated and registered the stockpiles of artificial silk yarn and finished piece goods, as well as the ramie silk on the machines, in various textile factories in Tianjin but had not released them. The customs also ordered the payment of taxes on the ramie silk for our piece goods, which has greatly affected the industry. As it was late, they did not get to meet with the responsible personnel. On the morning of the 2nd, they went to the Ministry of Finance to submit their petition in person and met with Wu Jing, chief of the Customs Administration Section of the Customs Service, to express their grievances and request: 1. The 244,105 pieces of stockpiled piece goods have been registered in accordance with the Ministry's order. Please order the customs to issue transportation and sales licenses as soon as possible. 2. Please grant a tax exemption for the ramie silk used for the piece goods on the machines. 3. For the stockpiled artificial silk, except for those with customs receipts, please complete the tax payment in accordance with the Ministry's order. Please approve this in order to relieve the difficulties of the merchants. According to Ba Lunquan, there are a total of 296 weaving factories in Tianjin, with more than 9,000 looms and more than 100,000 workers. Since these piece goods cannot be transported and sold, the factories have had to painfully suspend operations, incurring heavy losses, and the workers' lives have fallen into misery. This trip to Beijing is not only to appeal on behalf of the factories but also on behalf of the workers. (Special dispatch from the 2nd)
