Japan's Policy Towards China: From Military to Diplomatic, From Political to Economic

Tokyo Dispatch: After arriving in Tokyo, the most common slogan we heard was "Establish a diplomatic national policy." We found this truly surprising. Did Japan not have a "diplomatic national policy" before the September 18th Incident? Has Japan still not had a "diplomatic national policy" since the September 18th Incident? If it truly has not, then what has guided Japan's diplomatic work in these past five years? From "scorched earth diplomacy" to "harmonious diplomacy," hasn't Japan fully demonstrated its diplomatic guiding spirit on the world stage? The more we pondered, the less we understood. After much observation, we came to a conclusion: the so-called call to "establish a diplomatic national policy" arises from the following two viewpoints: First, some enlightened people deeply feel that the existing diplomatic national policy contains many dangers. Without fundamental reform, it will inevitably encounter enormous difficulties. Second, some enlightened people also keenly feel that to implement the existing diplomatic national policy, it is necessary to simultaneously expand the army, navy, and air force. The burden of military expenses is too heavy, and the development of industry will naturally be severely squeezed. Furthermore, other necessary administrative tasks will be affected by financial difficulties and cannot be realized quickly. Therefore, they call for a change in diplomatic national policy. The word "establish" used under these two viewpoints is actually a substitute for "change" or "reform."

What is Japan's current diplomatic national policy? This question is difficult for us to answer. Diplomatic national policy inherently contains secrecy, and it is naturally not something we can know. However, judging from national actions, it is not impossible to infer some fragments. Japan's diplomatic national policy—by carefully observing its attitude towards the Soviet Union, China, Britain, and the United States—seems not impossible to understand. This does not need our explanation. Recently, Foreign Minister Arita indirectly responded to society's demands for a definite diplomatic national policy in a cabinet meeting. Although not very detailed, we can see its trend. Foreign Minister Arita said, "We have a diplomatic national policy. We take dealing with the Soviet Union as the center of our diplomatic national policy. Because policy toward China is related to policy toward the Soviet Union, it must also be handled cautiously." At the same time, the army also said, "Japan's diplomatic national policy has long been determined. Now it is just a matter of implementation. Military strength is the basic condition for diplomacy, so military expansion is necessary." The statements of both the Foreign Ministry and the Army are very clear. However, Foreign Minister Arita's words only stated one aspect; another aspect is implied. In our view, the military aspect is naturally centered on dealing with the Soviet Union, while the political and economic aspects are naturally centered on dealing with China. Dealing with the Soviet Union and China are mutually causal. Because of the need to deal with the Soviet Union, China must be treated cautiously. Because of the need to deal with China, the Soviet Union must be treated cautiously. To go a step further, policy toward China is the center of Japan's diplomatic national policy. Policy towards the Soviet Union, Britain, and the United States all arise from this. People who have studied Japan's diplomatic history for the past sixty years can assert this. Therefore, when we understand Japan's policy toward China, we can recognize the entirety of Japan's diplomatic national policy.

After the resolution of the Southwestern Rebellion, Japanese people's views toward China gradually changed. This is a fact. They had always believed that China absolutely had no ability to unify and would forever be in chaos. Therefore, Japan did not need to observe China from the perspective of an entire nation. All kinds of policies toward China came from this fundamental theory. However, recently, because the Guangdong forces collapsed too quickly and internal strife has almost disappeared in the past five years, and the cause of unification has now reached about 90%, they gradually recognized that China's future for unification does not have great difficulties, and its strength of unity is not weak. Therefore, calls for re-examining policy toward China arose simultaneously in various circles. We will cite several examples for readers to see. Mr. Takagi Rikuro is one of the leading "China experts" among Japanese capitalists. On August 15, he published an article titled "Recent Movements in China" in "Diplomatic Times," and in the September issue of "Bungei Shunju," he published an article titled "Chiang Kai-shek's Financial Network." The main ideas of the two articles are the same, listing the progress of China's railways, highways, aviation, banking system, currency reform, postal savings, political control, scientific application, etc., in recent years, hoping that Japanese people will re-recognize China. He said, "People who only know the old China, discussing Japan's policy toward China, on the contrary, cause Japan to make mistakes. This is my frequent feeling." Mr. Sogawa Shinji is the president of the Yu-Zhong Company, which operates in Hebei, and is also a "China expert." He published an article titled "The Turning Point of Policy Toward China" in the September issue of "Bungei Shunju." He said, "If Japan only wants to have everything it asks for, then there is no need to say anything. But if we recognize China as our brotherly country, supporting each other, stabilizing East Asia, and increasing the welfare of the people, then the past policy toward China cannot but be said to be a failure. Japan asks China to reflect, but Japan should also clear away everything of the past, returning to a blank slate, and reforming policy toward China from the very first step is most necessary." He also said, "In short, whether Japanese soldiers, diplomats, civilian researchers, or China specialists, if they do not observe from the overall situation of the world, and regard the China problem as a world problem, merely confined to within the four hundred-odd states, observing China, discussing China, this is a fundamental error. They not only forget the world, but also do not have sufficient contact with the Chinese people in China. Their targets are only the warlords' powerful figures, and the local bullies and gentry-style capitalist compradores whom the people despise. They even believe that if they can manipulate them to serve Japan's current interests, they are confident that they are pursuing a policy toward China." This is a very fair argument. The famous Japanese reporter Ota Unosuke wrote an article titled "China Will Complete Its Unification" in the September issue of "Nippon Hyoron." He concluded by saying, "If China has no peace, then East Asia has no peace. If China is not unified, then China has no peace. If China does not have complete independence, then there is no true cooperation between China and Japan. Today is the time for Japan to change its view of China and even its view of the world." We believe that this is an immortal saying. We have never seen this kind of argument in the past five years. Ishimaru Tota is a well-known commentator among Japanese naval officers (now retired). In his new book "The Next World War," he discusses the causes of the future world war. In the chapter "Examining Japan-Soviet-China Relations," he said, "International relations are only about interests, and the center of promoting interests is the principle of give and take in diplomacy. In other words, when 'giving' and 'taking' can maintain balance, friendly relations can be maintained between the two countries. If not, relations will inevitably become estranged, eventually leading to 'taking' without 'giving,' developing into hostile relations... If China and Japan cannot maintain a balanced state of 'giving' and 'taking,' isn't it natural for China to adopt the policy of using barbarians to control barbarians? Therefore, asking China to reflect is truly nonsense from outsiders who do not know the basics of diplomacy." In the chapter "Can the Pacific War Be Avoided?" he also said, "Some say that the National Government's pro-Japan stance is fake. Please watch as it immediately takes off its mask and resists Japan again. As if seeing through Chiang's belly, they shout loudly, 'Power! Power! For China, power is the first. Only with power can China be subdued.' From the beginning, it is a fighting spirit. Then what is there to turn to or not turn to? It can be said that diplomacy is fundamentally useless. What is there to say about Sino-Japanese friendship work?' These conflicting opinions form a double diplomacy, which is truly Japan's misfortune." This person's argument is truly extremely sharp. He also said, "Which side China stands on in the next world war depends on Japan's attitude. If China and Japan can truly achieve the goal of cooperation, the Japan-US and Japan-Soviet wars may even be avoided. In any case, Japan's attitude is the decisive factor." His vision is broad and his observation is thorough. We can only admire him. The Osaka Mainichi and Tokyo Nichinichi newspapers, which have always seemed to hold a prejudice against the China problem, have also gradually turned around in the past half month. Isn't this hinting at a change in the times? However, readers should not be too optimistic. Although this kind of argument can gradually be seen in society, the timing is probably not yet ripe for it to gain decisive power in diplomacy and politics.

We have quoted many arguments, which seems to have deviated from the topic. So, has there really been a change in the substance of the Japanese government's policy toward China? It is very obvious that there is a shift from military work to diplomatic work, and from political work to economic work. The first thing Ambassador Kawagoe said upon taking office was the "theory of economic cooperation." After Foreign Minister Arita took office, he also emphasized the necessity of "economic diplomacy." These are all worthy of our attention. Japan is currently encountering many difficulties in trade and is hitting walls everywhere. If it does not open up a path from the economic aspect, not only will international trade be greatly affected, but domestic industry and commerce will also suffer related deterioration. Paying attention to the economic development of Hebei is one reason. Using Hebei's rich resources to enrich Japan's broader national defense and increase Japan's industry and commerce is an unbeatable strategy. Japan's view of China seems to be a little different recently. The Southwestern problem was a huge turning point. They know that China is not "Wu Xia Ameng." The central control is powerful. The form of the entire country is complete. The era of diplomatic work based on various localities has passed. China's target is only one National Government. Therefore, the requirements to resolve pending issues, reduce tariffs, economic cooperation methods, etc., must all be negotiated through diplomatic channels. Restoring diplomatic normalcy cannot but be said to be a preliminary improvement. Japan feels the necessity of unifying diplomacy, perhaps to the same extent as China. Although the issue of unifying diplomacy has been pending for 30 years, judging from the facts of the past five years, both countries' enlightened people particularly keenly feel that correction is a matter of urgency. Efforts were made in the Hirota era, but unfortunately, they did not achieve much. In the Arita era, further efforts must of course be made to achieve it. Under the current situation, the degree of unification seems to have reached 70%. There is still a key issue that has not been completely resolved. Currently, within the cabinet, the foreign, army, and navy ministers are sure to gather after the cabinet meeting every week to discuss the problems of China and the Soviet Union. They often discuss them, and their opinions are easily unified. The environment for unification is much better than before. If the central government and those abroad can completely agree, then unified diplomacy can be realized. We earnestly hope that China and Japan first restore diplomatic normalcy, and then talk about concrete problems. I am afraid that many enlightened people in Japan hold the same opinion. Today, people in the country want to ask what Japan's policy toward China is. We have only one answer. The famous reporter Ota said, "Only when China has complete independence can there be true cooperation between China and Japan." In the same style, we want to say, "Only when China has an entire nation can Japan have a rational policy toward China."

The Guangdong-Hankou Railway Officially Opens to Traffic: Direct Journey in 44 Hours, Opening Ceremony Scheduled for Double Tenth Festival

Hankou Dispatch: The Guangdong-Hankou Railway, which the whole country has been looking forward to, has now officially opened to direct traffic. The construction of this road has a history of 35 years and has great significance in terms of politics, economy, culture, and national defense. It not only connects the north and south but also facilitates transportation. The first express train started from Guangzhou on September 1, and from Wuchang on the 4th. The train numbers are designated as No. 41 southbound and No. 42 northbound. From then on, express trains will run north and south every Tuesday and Friday, requiring 44 hours for the entire journey. In the future, it can be shortened to 36 hours. The fare is calculated at 1.25 cents per kilometer, with third-class at $13.70, second-class at $27.40, and first-class at $41.20. The special express train between Wuchang and Hengyang still runs as usual every night. The Railway Bureau stipulates that a station be set up in Hengzhou, but currently it is temporarily set up in Wuchang. Director Ling Hongxun has gone south to preside over the grand opening ceremony to be held in Wuchang on the Double Tenth Festival. The construction history, construction progress, reorganization of the Railway Bureau, unification of railway administration, and stations, scenery, and products along the way are investigated in detail and recorded on the left, which I think is also what the people of the country want to hear.

The Construction Process of the Guangdong-Hankou Railway

The Guangdong-Hankou Railway is the only trunk line in South China, spanning the three provinces of Hubei, Hunan, and Guangdong. It starts from Wuchang in the north and ends in Guangzhou in the south, with a total length of 1,090 kilometers. Ten years ago, the Englishman Stephen first proposed the idea of building the road, and it was not approved until 1898. The Sino-American Development Company undertook the construction. In that year, the Spanish-American War was extended, and construction began in the autumn of the following year. After only surveying, the budget of 4 million pounds was insufficient for wages, and it stopped because of a request to revise the contract. In the spring of 1900, the government completed the revision of the contract. In 1902, the Guangzhou to Sanshui line via Foshan began construction. In 1904, the Guangzhou-Sanshui line was completed. At that time, Belgium planned to sign a treaty with our country, but it was rejected by the Chinese people. Then came the American Morgan Company, which was opposed by the Chinese people. The government then gave 6,750,000 gold dollars, with 3,750,000 gold dollars as interest losses and 3,000,000 gold dollars as compensation for suspension of work, canceling the contract with the American company. This kind of contract compensation was then borrowed from the Hong Kong government for pounds, the so-called Wuchang loan of 1906. Afterwards, Chinese people raised funds to organize a company to continue construction. In 1915, the section from Guangzhou to was completed. The northern section, Hubei, obtained the British Hubei-Guangdong Railway loan and also built from Wuchang to the Hunan border. Construction started in the first year of the Republic of China and stopped due to the outbreak of war. Later, the northern section was extended to Changsha, with a length of 417 kilometers, all of which were the Hunan-Hubei Railway. The southern section from Guangzhou to had a length of 213 kilometers, named the Yue-Shaoguan Railway, while the middle section, Zhuzhou to Shaoguan, was 450 kilometers long, accounting for 40% of the remaining road. The Zhushao Road from was difficult, with a vast project, lasting up to 11 years. In the autumn of the 22nd year of the Republic, the Ministry of Railways of the National Government intended to use the Boxer Indemnity and the income from the southern section for construction, proposing 1.66 million pounds for the purchase of materials abroad and 30 million yuan for the purchase of materials and wages in the country. The project then proceeded smoothly, and today the entire line is open to direct traffic. The northern road can be a state-owned railway trunk line with the unanimous efforts of the court and the public. In the future, after connecting with the Pinghan Railway, it can go south to Guangzhou and north to Beiping. We are very pleased to see the entire line open to traffic today.

Progress of the Zhushao Section Project

The Zhushao section project is the most difficult in the entire road. It accounts for three-quarters in Hunan Province and one-quarter in Guangdong Province. In the 22nd year of the Republic, the Ministry of Railways decided to complete the road and appointed Ling Hongxun as the director and chief engineer of the Zhushao section. The bureau was set up on the east bank of the Xiangjiang River in Hengyang, and the Zhushao section project was scheduled to be completed in four years. In fact, construction has been underway to date. Because of phased construction and scientific management, it was completed in only two years and eight months. The funds used were borrowed by the Ministry of Railways from the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Committee. Domestic construction funds used 38,332,000 yuan, and foreign material funds used 1,645,000 pounds, totaling 60 million national currency. The estimated price per kilometer is about 150,000 yuan. Steel rails were purchased from the United Kingdom. North of Hengzhou, medicine-treated American pine was used for sleepers, and south of Hengzhou, hard rosewood was used. The roadbed is made of red soil from open mountains, which is the most viscous. Stone ballast uses pebbles from the Xiangjiang River, or crushed stones from open mountains are paved, which is very suitable. There are many outstanding projects. The most difficult ones for the construction industry are the mountains and valleys, including Jinlong Mountain, Jiaowan, Yantang, the Guangdong-Hunan border, Chong, and three. In Hengyang North, there are three major steel bridges: the steel bridge, 240.6 meters long, the Xiangjiang River, 397 meters long, and the Xiangjiang River Bridge, 439.5 meters long. The large arch bridges are the Xin Yanxia Bridge, the Dui Chong Bridge, the Provincial Boundary Bridge, the Fengkou Bridge, and the Yantang Bridge. There are a total of 1,322 bridges and culverts of various types, with a construction cost of more than 12 million yuan. The speed of construction and the greatness of the results are second only to the Jing-Sui Road (Jing-Zhang section) completed by Zhan Tianyou. From this, it can be seen that my country's engineering community has made significant progress.

Reorganizing the Railway Bureau and Unifying Railway Administration

The Guangdong-Hankou Railway, due to the obstruction of the Zhushao section, has not been open to traffic for a long time, and management is divided into three sections: the Guangzhou-Shaoguan in the south, the Hunan-Hubei in the north, and each has its own management bureau, and the Zhushao in the middle has an engineering bureau. In recent years, the Ministry of Railways has established the Guangdong-Hankou Railway Planning and Organizing Committee. Although it is a design agency, the unity of the entire road has begun to take shape. On August 1 this year, the Ministry ordered the reorganization of the committee into the Guangdong-Hankou Railway Organizing Committee, with Chen Yanjiong as the chairman, Li Xian'gen, Yin Deyang, and Ling Hongxun as standing committee members. The three section bureaus were abolished and reorganized into the Guangdong-Hankou Railway Administration, with Ling Hongxun as the director and Zhou Zhongqi and Wang Renkang as his deputies. The characteristics of its organization are that there is no train affairs and machinery affairs department, and a transport affairs department is set up to manage the original train affairs and machinery affairs departments' driving management and vehicle dispatch, so as to achieve the effect of locomotive cooperation. A business office is set up to take charge of passenger and freight business and water and land combined transport, so as to seek the commercialization of the railway. A factory affairs office is also added, with a total of six major offices. Liu Chenghou is the director of the general affairs office, and Qu Jiaying is the deputy director. The office is responsible for six sections: writing, personnel, industry and health, affairs, materials, and the material factory. Chen Xiaogang is the director of the transport affairs office, and Feng Jian is the deputy director. The office is responsible for four sections: transfer, transport affairs, mechanics, and accounting, and the transport station. Zhou Zhongqi is the director of the business office, and Kaihua is responsible for the passenger and freight sections and the business station. Li Guo is the director of the engineering office, and Wen is the deputy director. The office is responsible for the construction and design sections and the engineering section and the engineering. Zi is the director of the factory affairs office, and Cheng Wenxi is the deputy director. The office is responsible for the management and sections and the factory. Cao is the director, and is responsible for the sections. A liaison office is set up in Guangzhou and is responsible for the and sections. Therefore, the regulations are unified, and the authority can be concentrated. The vehicles purchased by the bureau are ordered from the United Kingdom, including 28 locomotives, 50 passenger cars, including 5 first-class sleeping cars, 5 second-class sleeping cars, 5 dining cars, 5 baggage cars, 5 mail cars, and 425 freight cars, which are enough to equip 5 passenger trains to run on the entire line. Most of the various vehicles have been shipped, and the rest will be shipped to Wuchang for installation before the Double Tenth Festival.

Stations, Scenery, and Products Along the Way

The railway stations from Wuchang to Guangzhou are Xujiapeng, Tongxiangmen, Yujiawan, Zhifang, Tuditang, Shanpo, Heshengqiao, Guanbuqiao, Xianning, Tingsiqiao, Zhonghuopoo, Putai, Chaanling, Zhaoliqiao, Yanglousi, Linxiang, Lukoupoo, Yunxi, Chenglingji, Yuezhou, Matang, Rongjiawan, Huangshajie, Taolin Temple, Miluo, Baishui, Gaojiafang, Qiaotoubu, Xiani, Changshabei, Changshadong, Dabeipoo, Lujiawan, Zhuzhou, Kou, Sanmen, Zhaoling, Jinkou, Zhuting, Shiwan, Hengshan, Xialiushi, Tianerbu, Hengzhou, Dongyangdu, Guanyinqiao, Wa, Zheqiao, Leiyang, Xiaoshuipoo, Gongpingxu, Gaotingsi, Qifengdu, Xujiadong, Chenzhou, Chenshang, Dengjiatang, Taipingli, Baishidu, Pingshi, Luojiadu, Qimen, Lechang, Yangxi, Liputou, Hebianchang, Shaozhou, Maba, Wushi, Dakengkou, Shakou, Hetou, Yingde, Boluokeng, Lianjiangkou, Tan, Yingzui, Yinzhan, Juntian, Letong, Xinjie, Guotang, Jiangcun, Dalang, Xiaocun, Xicun, Huangsha, a total of ninety stations. Now, Xujiapeng is renamed Wuchang East Station, Tongxiangmen is renamed Wuchang Main Station, Chenzhou is renamed Chenxian Station, Hengzhou is renamed Hengyang Station, Shaozhou is renamed Qujiang Station, Xicun is renamed Guangzhou West Station, and Huangsha is renamed Guangzhou South Station. The products along the line are abundant, such as rice and minerals in Hunan, oil cakes, grains, tea, cowhide, homespun cloth, and eggs in Hubei, and food and seafood in Guangdong, which can be supplied to each other in the future. Taking Xiang rice as an example, if it can be sold in Guangdong, it can reach 2.4 million bags per year, which is enough to make up for the 10 million yuan annual leakage of Guangdong purchasing foreign rice, and Guangdong transporting and selling to Hunan can also regulate the people's food. Therefore, the opening of this road is of great significance to the national economy and the people's livelihood. As for the scenic spots, there are too many to list. The mountains include the 72 peaks of Mount Heng, and the rivers include the Yangtze River, Dongting Lake, Xiang River, Wu River, and North River. Yuezhou has Yueyang Tower and Little Qiao's Tomb, Miluo is where Qu Yuan drowned, Leiyang has Zhang's horse drinking trough, the location of the garrison, and the tomb of Du Fu. In Lechang, Han Yu of Changli once lived as an official, and the plaque "Kites fly and fish leap" that he personally inscribed is still majestic. Famous ministers, poets, and heroes have left their mark for thousands of years, which is enough for people to look up to and pay their respects.

Songjiang: Escaped Prisoner Recaptured

He Houren, a robbery convict from Dongtai detained in the county prison, was sentenced to eight years in prison. Recently, he was assigned to do outside labor carrying mud for house repairs. He took advantage of the guard's carelessness and escaped. By the time the guard realized it, he had disappeared without a trace. The matter was reported to the Public Security Bureau by the prison official, and orders were issued to investigate and arrest him. Eventually, he was spotted by a guard from the prison at the Mingxing Bridge Station. The prisoner fled, but was stopped and detained, and taken back for interrogation.

Kunshan: County Magistrate Prays for Good Harvest

In recent years, the county has suffered repeated disasters and poor autumn harvests. This year, the county's farmland has hopes for a good harvest of early rice, and the late rice also presents an optimistic outlook. The villagers have been celebrating the good harvest enthusiastically. County Magistrate Peng Baichuan specially prayed for a good harvest in the whole county at the Huazang Temple on Ma'an Mountain on the Zhongyuan Festival (30th). The ceremony was grand, and all the great lay Buddhists of the Lotus Society attended, which was quite a grand occasion.

Suzhou: Adjusting Disputes Between Landlords and Tenants

County Magistrate Deng Xianghai, in order to adjust the disputes between landlords and tenants in Wu County, convened a meeting on the morning of the 1st with all parties concerned and representatives of the industry guilds to discuss together. In the afternoon of that day, the landlords exchanged opinions again at the Tianye Business Office. On the morning of the 2nd, a meeting was held again at the county government, chaired by County Magistrate Deng, to conduct a detailed study of important issues such as industry guild registration. As a result of the two-day consultation, agreements were reached on major issues such as disaster investigation, rent payment, discount, relief to farmers, disposition of land rent, industry guild registration, and rural relief. The county government will submit a report to the province for approval. The date for rent payment will be determined and announced by the county government and the county party headquarters. The industry guild bill will be changed to a notification bill. Rent collection shall not exceed 85% of the original rent. Disaster investigation shall be carried out when the rice is ripe but not harvested, and a disaster investigation committee shall be organized in each township. Industry guild registration shall be handled by the county government. Rent rice discount shall be determined by the county government and the county party headquarters based on the average price of Suzhou new coarse japonica rice from the date of early rice listing to the day after the first frost. All industry guilds must comply with it. As for cracking down on urging and collection, it will be temporarily suspended. The issue of paying salaries to urging officials was not studied because it concerned the county budget.

Changshu: Vegetable Industry Opposes Excessive Taxes

The local tax bureau of Changshu County recently resumed the collection of taxes on hotels, restaurants, and tea houses, prompting opposition from these businesses. On the evening of September 1st, an emergency meeting was convened, and the situation appeared quite serious, potentially leading to a market strike by these businesses. This area began levying taxes on hotels, restaurants, and tea houses in the spring of the 23rd year of the Republic (1934) due to insufficient public security funds. The tax amount was determined by each establishment, with a total annual collection of 2,400 yuan. Initially, the monthly revenue was only over 30 yuan, barely enough to cover the living expenses of one tax collector, and due to the trivial nature of the matter, it was virtually abolished. This has continued for twenty-five months. Unexpectedly, the county government, noting the prolonged absence of this tax collection, reappointed Bian as the tax collector. Accompanied by bailiffs, he pursued the twenty-five months of arrears from the businesses. Those who resisted had their managers detained. Consequently, the businesses held an emergency meeting to petition the county party headquarters and the chamber of commerce, seeking justice and proposing two points:

To waive the arrears of the past twenty-five months.

To temporarily suspend collection pending a resolution from the provincial government. At that time, the chamber of commerce agreed to petition the provincial government on their behalf to strive for the abolition of the excessive taxes. Currently, these three industries are organizing a temporary consortium. If the county government insists on strict collection, they will respond by organizing a market strike and business closures.

Wuxi: Impersonating an Official to Defraud Money Leads to Imprisonment

Zhao, a resident of No. 105 Beidang in this county, possesses considerable wealth and has two sons. The elder son, Zhicheng, received higher education, while the younger son, Zhili, graduated from Nanjing Central University. However, Zhicheng did not engage in proper work and indulged in wandering. His father's attempts to discipline him were ineffective, leading to a newspaper announcement severing their father-son relationship. After leaving home, Zhicheng associated with hooligans, specializing in extortion. At the end of 1933, Zhao, dressed in military uniform and wearing a military belt, encountered Li Jianleng, a native of Dongyang County, Jinhua, Zhejiang, in Nanjing. Zhao claimed to be the district chief of the supervisory audit office in Jiangxi to Shanxi, stating that he could recommend Li as a battalion commander if he was interested, but a security deposit of 500 yuan was required. Li, believing this to be true, raised 500 silver dollars and gave them to Zhao Zhicheng, who then issued a letter of appointment. After receiving the letter, Li immediately returned to Shanghai to prepare for taking up the position in Jiangxi. However, the unit stated that they had not appointed Li as a battalion commander and that they had never heard of Zhao Zhicheng. Li was detained and sent to the Nanchang headquarters for strict handling. It was at this point that Li realized he had been deceived. After explaining the situation, Li was released from prison. Recently, Zhao also defrauded Zhang Jisheng of 1,000 yuan in legal tender in Hangzhou and fled to Wuxi. After Li Jianleng found out about this, he went to Wuxi from Shanghai with his younger brother, Li Chao, and his wife, Gu Jingjun, and apprehended Zhao on the street. He was sent to the Second Branch of the Public Security Bureau in charge and transferred to the General Bureau. Zhao directly admitted to impersonating an official to defraud money. Yesterday, he was transferred to the court, and after interrogation by the procurator, he was ordered to be detained pending investigation.

Nantong: Drug Trafficking Den Uncovered in Jinsha

The Public Security Bureau uncovered a drug trafficking ring in Jiepai Town on the border of Jinsha Yanlu Township and seized morphine. Seven drug offenders, including Shan Hairu, were apprehended, and the witnesses were all sent to the Fourth District Security Command for interrogation.

District Chief Pu Liu Assaulted

Wei Huai, the district chief of Pu Liu in the Third District of Tongyi, went to stop a witch god gathering held by the villagers of Xifang Township late at night. He was surrounded by the villagers and beaten, sustaining injuries. He was rescued by the security team, and the county government apprehended the main instigators, Wu and Wu Jincheng, for interrogation.

Haizhou: Township Head Flees to Evade Punishment

Liu Hairu, the township head of Wenhua Township in the Second District of this county, previously harbored bandits and concealed bandit guns. The security team repeatedly searched for him without success. Subsequently, the district office requested and was approved by the county government to dismiss him, and Liu Daoli, the head of the fourth bao in the township, was recommended to replace him. However, after the bandit collusion case occurred, Liu Hairu fled with the official seal to evade punishment. This prevented the new township head from taking office. The district office has now requested the county government to issue a strict arrest warrant and reissue the township office seal to enable its use and ensure credibility.

Hangzhou: Feng Yuxiang Gives Instructions in Hangzhou

Feng Yuxiang, Deputy Chairman of the Military Affairs Commission, arrived in Hangzhou from Nanchang at 8:00 AM on the 1st and went to Hai Ning to watch the tide at Ba. He was entertained by the Provincial Party Headquarters and the Provincial Government in the evening, and stayed at the China Bank Villa. Over 1,000 staff members from various departments and bureaus attended. Xu Qingfu gave an introductory speech, followed by Feng Yuxiang's instructions, which mainly covered two points:

Zhejiang Province's implementation of the New Life Movement surpasses all other regions.

The Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway is more economical, cleaner, and more orderly than the Longhai Railway. At 9:00 AM, he visited the Jianqiao Aviation School, and returned to the city at 11:30 AM. He gave a speech to the youth at the lecture hall. At 12:30 PM, he went to the Wuxing Gospel Hospital to visit Old Mrs. Meng, and then went to Jiaxing Cheng Dian. A specially prepared train carried his secretary and guards, departing at 2:00 PM and arriving in Jiaxing at 3:00 PM. Ningbo: Armed Fight Over Fish Theft

Kandun Town in Yuyao, about sixty li from the city, is adjacent to Shengshan and Baisha. On the afternoon of the 10th of last month, Yang Baorong and Yang Yaocan, villagers from Jiepai Tou, went to the Dihe Lake to steal fish raised by the Xu family. They were discovered by Xu Abing, Xu Huiren, and others, who gathered more than ten people, confiscated the fishing nets, and pushed the Yangs into the lake. The Yangs, unwilling to accept this, gathered more than twenty people to reason with them. However, Xu Abing and others learned of this and rang gongs to gather more than two hundred villagers, each armed with weapons, who rushed to Kandun and blocked the Yangs' path. A fight broke out, and villager Chen Zhaochang's lower abdomen was stabbed by Xu Huiren with a sharp blade, causing profuse bleeding and endangering his life. Fortunately, the local security corps arrived and suppressed the situation, and peace was restored.

The Boundary Demarcation of Shengsi is Approaching

The long-pending issue of the boundary demarcation of the Shengsi Islands has not yet been resolved after joint inspections by officials from Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces. Last month, the Shanghai native place associations of Ningbo, Dinghai, and Fenghua, citing the Provincial and County Boundary Survey Regulations promulgated by the Executive Yuan in 1930, and based on geography, submitted separate petitions to the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Interior, requesting boundary demarcation according to the map and ordering the Jiangsu and Zhejiang provincial governments to hand over the area as soon as possible, so that the long-pending case could be resolved soon. It is now known that the Executive Yuan, after receiving the petitions, has scheduled a boundary demarcation meeting in Nanjing on September 4th, and has telegraphed the Jiangsu and Zhejiang provincial governments to inform them. After receiving the telegram, the Zhejiang Provincial Government has telegraphed Commissioner Zhao of the Yin District to represent them at the meeting in Nanjing. It is said that Zhao plans to travel to Nanjing via the province to attend the boundary demarcation meeting.

The Ministry of Finance is Planning to Print its own Banknotes; Approves a Special Request from the Municipal Assembly

The First Special District Citizens' Federation of this city, recognizing the diverse and difficult-to-identify banknotes in circulation and the urgent need for unified issuance and purchase of printing machines to reclaim rights and interests, resolved at its seventh executive committee meeting to petition the Ministry of Finance for implementation. It is now learned that the federation received a reply from the Ministry of Finance yesterday, Qianzi No. 10601, which stated, "Reply to the Shanghai First Special District Citizens' Federation's petition on August 11, 1936, regarding the difficulty in identifying the various banknotes in circulation and requesting approval and implementation of the three proposed measures. The petition has been noted. The three proposed measures are indeed essential. Since the implementation of the legal tender, this ministry has repeatedly issued orders to the four banks (Central, China, Communications, and Farmers) to display sample banknotes for identification by the local people in order to facilitate the identification of genuine and counterfeit banknotes. As for the banknotes issued by banks other than the four banks (Central, China, Communications, and Farmers) before the implementation of the legal tender, many have already been recovered and can be gradually recovered completely. As for the independent procurement of printing machines and the unification of banknote designs, it is currently under overall planning. Please take note of this reply."

Cathay Bank Urges Withdrawal of Deposits; Principal and Interest to be Fully Refunded

The Cathay Commercial Savings Bank of this city, in view of the depressed market conditions, difficulties in capital utilization, and lack of confidence in its operations, convened a shareholders' meeting and unanimously resolved to liquidate and dissolve the bank. All fixed and current deposit principals and interest will be fully refunded, and outstanding debts will be pursued. The bank's notice urging depositors to withdraw their deposits is as follows: Respectfully, this bank, through a resolution passed at the second extraordinary shareholders' meeting on August 30th of this year, has decided to liquidate and dissolve the bank, and has entrusted the entire board of directors to serve as liquidators. All fixed and current deposits in the commercial and savings departments, whether or not they have matured, are requested to come to the bank immediately to withdraw both principal and interest. Interest will be calculated up to the day before the withdrawal. This notice is hereby given. Depositors are respectfully requested to bring their deposit slips and follow the usual procedures for withdrawal. Your early visit is eagerly awaited.

Jianguo Refloats Itself and Returns to Shanghai Yesterday Morning; Enters the Factory for Repairs Today

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Changjiang steamer Jianguo ran aground on the Qingtian Reef. The Jiangshun steamer rescued more than 180 passengers and returned them to Shanghai. However, the Jianghua steamer's attempt to tow the ship was ineffective. While a steamer was being dispatched for rescue, the Wheeldock tugboat dispatched by the Shanghai Bureau and the three barges prepared for unloading the cargo had not yet arrived at the Qingtian Reef at 2:00 AM yesterday. However, the tide had risen greatly (the 12th and 3rd were spring tides). At 2:06 AM, the water had risen by four English feet, and the combined water volume exceeded thirteen feet. The draft of the Jianguo after loading was only twelve feet six inches. At this time, the bow of the grounded ship had automatically floated up, and the damaged rudder screw had also been repaired. When the ship reached Huang Youshi, it did not wait for the Wheeldock tugboat to arrive and did not need to unload the cargo. It was able to get off the shoal. It urgently reversed the engine and left the shoal on its own, returning to Shanghai. It entered the port at about 9:00 AM. After the ship arrived in Shanghai, the shipowner Huang reported the process to the Bureau. The Bureau sent an engineer to inspect the ship and then unloaded the cargo. It will enter the factory for repairs today.

Mu Xiangyue Bitterly Discusses the New Special Goods Tax; Sends Telegrams to Nanjing and Hebei Authorities

Mu Xiangyue telegraphed to Nanjing and Hebei authorities yesterday, saying, "To President Jiang of the Nanjing Executive Yuan, Minister Kong of the Ministry of Finance, and Minister Wu of the Ministry of Industry: A telegram was recently sent to Chairman Song Zheyuan of the Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Council in Beiping, which reads, 'To Chairman Song Mingxuan of the Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Council and all members: Reports indicate that your council will impose a new tax on special goods transported into Hebei-Chahar, equivalent to one-eighth of the national customs duty, which is deeply concerning and confusing. This move is equivalent to transforming what was previously considered smuggled goods by the customs into legitimate imports, which can be freely transported within the country without any obstacles. This is tantamount to undermining the uniformity of customs administration, destroying the revival of domestic industry, suppressing the development of the national economy, and disrupting the national fiscal budget. The economic aggression is more brutal than military force. Your Excellency supports the precarious situation with painstaking efforts, and your patriotic sincerity is admired by all. A man of your wisdom would not do this. However, if this is implemented, the lifeline of the country and the livelihood of the people will be completely ruined. Please do your best to mediate and abolish this measure to leave a glimmer of hope for the national economy. I had the pleasure of meeting you once, and I cannot bear to see your reputation tarnished. I have taken the liberty of making these remarks, and I hope you will reply. Mu Xiangyue, seal,' etc. Please review and approve this and immediately stop it. The country will be very fortunate. Mu Xiangyue, seal.'"

For the past three or four years, it has been occupied by Communist bandits who have been committing arson, murder, looting, and all sorts of atrocities in the countryside, causing the good people to be alarmed and unable to sleep peacefully. What have our people done to deserve such suffering? The autumn harvest is approaching, and the people's food supply is at stake. I, Xiaoya, grew up in this village and have seen and heard more about this. The current bandits are mostly a rabble that cannot withstand a single blow. Only a brigade of troops is needed to attack from Kaihua, Deyu, and the eastern villages of Wuyuan to encircle them on three sides, and it would not be difficult to annihilate them in one fell swoop. Your Excellency commands the troops and creates blessings for the people of the four provinces. Our county is also under your care. Because I have been living away from home for a long time, I cannot fully perform the duties of a host, and I feel very sorry. Now, I humbly represent the people of my county to plead for help, to quickly send elite troops to wipe out the Communist bandits and save the masses from this deep pit of suffering. The merit of this will be boundless. Respectfully wishing you a quick victory, Wang Xiaoya kowtows." (2) Mr. Zhang's reply telegram reads, "To Mr. Wang Xiaoya: Your telegram of the other day, informing me of the bandit disturbances in Wuyuan, has been received. Regulations for Changing the Name of Organizations Stipulated by the Central Ministry of People's Training

The Central Ministry of People's Training has promulgated the following methods for people's organizations to apply for changing their names: (1) People's organizations applying to change their names must follow the provisions of the change method. (2) People's organizations changing their names must be resolved by the general meeting of members and submit a letter of justification to the local senior party headquarters for approval. (3) After receiving the request, the party headquarters should carefully assess the situation and, if it believes that the reasons are sufficient and there is indeed a need to change the name, it should immediately approve the change and send a letter to the same-level government for reference. (4) After receiving approval, the people's organization should immediately prepare an application letter, along with the charter, membership list, and resumes of officials, and submit them separately to the original approving party headquarters and the competent government authority for registration. (5) After the party and government agencies approve the name change of the people's organization and file it for record, they should immediately apply for a change of seal in accordance with the law. (6) After the party and government agencies approve the name change of the people's organization, they should report it to the central competent department for record level by level. (7) These methods shall be promulgated and implemented by the Central Ministry of People's Training.

French Consulate Stipulates Rickshaw Limits; Limited to 34,000 People; Fee of 2 Jiao, Additional 5 Jiao

The French Consulate specially issued a decree yesterday regarding public rickshaw pullers and the issuance of rickshaw licenses, valid until September 1, 1936, and limited to 34,000 people. The license fee for public rickshaw pullers is 2 jiao per license. From September 1st onwards, the license fee for rickshaw pullers exceeding the 34,000 limit is 5 jiao per license. The duplicate of the rickshaw license is 2 jiao per license. Public rickshaw licenses should be exchanged annually between October 1st and December 31st, with an exchange fee of 2 jiao per license. However, licenses issued in the fourth quarter of 1936 may only be exchanged in 1937.

Bloodshed Erupts During Shanghai Municipal Council's Demolition of Shantytowns in Eastern Shanghai Yesterday Morning; Over Forty Shantytown Residents, Men and Women, Injured; Over Thirty People Arrested, Three Detectives Also Injured; United Association Holds Emergency Meeting, Demanding Release and Punishment of Culprits

According to the New Voice News Agency, the Shanghai Municipal Council sent detectives yesterday morning to forcibly demolish shantytowns in eastern Shanghai, resulting in a bloody tragedy. Over forty shantytown residents, men and women, were injured. On the detective side, one Western detective and two Indian detectives were also injured. After the incident, representatives were selected from the area to petition the Chinese directors of the Ratepayers' Association, the First Special District Citizens' United Association, and the Shanghai Municipal Council. At 4:00 PM, the Shanghai Shantytown United Association held an emergency meeting to discuss countermeasures, resolving to demand the immediate release of the arrested poor people and to punish the culprits and provide compensation. Details of the situation are recorded as follows:

Incident Circumstances

The incident was triggered by Shantytown No. 448 in the area. Due to the age and decay of the shacks, they were no longer habitable, and residents planned to repair them. However, the Shanghai Municipal Council intervened and stopped the repairs. Despite repeated requests for leniency from the shantytown residents, they were unsuccessful. At 9:15 AM yesterday morning, the Shanghai Municipal Council sent a large number of detectives and laborers to order the demolition. The shantytown residents, feeling a sense of shared fate, rushed to request leniency. However, a misunderstanding occurred at this moment. Batons flew, and many people fell to the ground injured. The shantytown women also fought back with chamber pots and washbasins, throwing excrement and other objects into the air, resulting in yellow and white substances splattered everywhere, and the stench was unbearable. Many shantytown residents were injured, and many were arrested on the spot and temporarily detained at the Yangshupu Police Station. According to subsequent investigations, over thirty people were arrested.

Separate Petitions

Feeling that the incident was unexpected and a complete disaster, the shantytown residents selected Ji Yunsheng, Tang Anping, Xu Xiguang, Duan Yifu, Zhang Buyun, Ruan Bukuan, Chen Qingde, Wang Daoyi, Zhu Yushu, and others to petition separately. They first went to the Chinese Ratepayers' Association on Hong Kong Road. After submitting their petition, the person in charge of the association inquired in detail about the incident and promised to find a way to negotiate. They then went to the First Special District Citizens' United Association at Tianhougong Bridge. Hu Fengxiang and Cao Zhigong, the executive members of the association, received them and also promised to provide assistance. The representatives left the Citizens' United Association at nearly 4:30 PM and went to the Shanghai Municipal Council again to demand the release of the arrested individuals.

Injury Investigation

Among the shantytown residents, over ten people were injured, including Gu Baotian, Gu Naiming, Sun Hankui, Pan Youji, Liu Yuming, Kuai Jiayan, Old Man Sun, Old Man Gao, Old Man Yang, and Mrs. Le, the mother of Jiang Beiyu. Over twenty people, including Zhou Xiaowu, sustained minor injuries. On the detective side, one Western detective and two Indian detectives were also injured. Currently, most of the injured shantytown residents have been arrested and are in the police station, while the remaining are moaning in their shacks, a truly tragic sight.

Emergency Meeting

The All-City Shantytown United Association held an emergency meeting of all executive committee members at its headquarters at 4:00 PM yesterday afternoon to discuss countermeasures for the case. Chairman Tang Anping resolved the following: How to negotiate with the Shanghai Municipal Council for forcibly demolishing the shacks of poor people and wantonly harming the working masses? Resolution: A. Send another letter to the Shanghai Municipal Council for serious negotiations. B. Send another letter to the Ratepayers' Association and the Citizens' Association, advocating for the protection of workers' lives and arguing based on reason. The association had previously sent a letter to the Shanghai Municipal Council proposing a gradual reduction in shacks and improvements in education and sanitation. Before receiving a reply, they recklessly acted, sending a large number of Chinese, Western, and Indian detectives and laborers to forcibly demolish the shacks on Chaoyang Road and indiscriminately injure civilians. How to negotiate this case? Resolution: A. Submit a serious negotiation to the Shanghai Municipal Council to stop the demolition. B. Detectives who have neglected their duties should be punished. C. Guarantee that similar incidents will not occur in the future. D. Release the detained civilians within 24 hours. E. The Shanghai Municipal Council should be responsible for medical expenses and compensation for losses for the injured. F. Send letters to all sectors of society, upholding justice and requesting unanimous assistance. How to provide relief to the families of the shantytown residents who were beaten and injured? Resolution: A. Send representatives to express condolences. Tang Anping, Ji Yunsheng, and Xu Xiguang are responsible. B. The association will temporarily provide subsidies as appropriate.

County Local Association Discusses Land Prices Yesterday

The Shanghai County's conversion of land tax to land value tax has been decided to be implemented this year. However, the County Local Association believed that the Land Bureau's assessment of farmland prices was too high and had repeatedly requested the provincial and county governments to reassess them, but without success. Therefore, the association held a meeting at the Beiqiao County Property Office at 10:00 AM yesterday. Over ten people, including Wang Chengyao, Zhang Jingye, and Wu Shifang, attended, with Chairman Qin Xitian presiding. After discussion, the attendees generally agreed that the land value tax in Jiangsu Province was only being piloted in Shanghai and Nanhui counties. Now that Nanhui has been delayed due to various reasons, and given the situation in this county, which affects the burden on the people of the entire county, it should also be delayed in order to reassess the land prices. Therefore, it was publicly resolved to submit a report to the provincial government's Land Bureau, requesting permission to delay the implementation in order to alleviate the people's hardship. At 2:00 PM, County Land Bureau Director Jin Yanze was invited to the meeting for discussions.

New Pharmaceutical Industry Corrects Private Meetings, Establishes Inspection Rules

The New Pharmaceutical Industry Association of this city, recognizing that the prevalence of smuggled goods is sufficient to affect the national economy, and that new drugs are mostly purchased from abroad, fearing that they are more easily mixed with smuggled goods, has appointed Xu Xiaochu, Zhou Bangjun, Xu Xiangsun, Yuan Hesong, Tu Zheng, Zhu Ruichen, and 17 other individuals to organize a private inspection committee. It is understood that the association has established inspection rules and ordered the industry to comply with and implement them. The rules are recorded as follows: Article 1: This association is established to prevent smuggled goods and protect the transportation and sale of legitimate goods. In accordance with the General Rules for Inspection by the Private Inspection Committee of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, these inspection rules are established. Article 2: This association may formulate methods for handling all inspection matters. Article 3: All members of the industry must complete a volunteer form, stating that they swear not to transport or sell smuggled goods, and the person in charge must sign and seal the form to show solemnity. Article 4: The inventory of members of the industry should be registered by obtaining a registration form from this association. The amount of the registration will be negotiated separately. Article 5: After the inventory is registered, the association will issue it to each group and send personnel to verify it. If no doubts arise, the stamp will be affixed and entered into the book for submission to the association for record. Article 6: When registered and verified inventory is transported to other places for sale, an application form must be completed and sent to the association, requesting proof of approval without doubt, and a certificate of proof will be issued for delivery with the goods. If sold to local members of the industry, only the number and name must be reported for verification. Article 7: If members of the industry do not follow the procedures in the preceding article, resulting in obstacles to the transportation and sale of goods, the association will not provide assistance. Article 8: If the association discovers that a member of the industry is transporting or selling smuggled goods, in addition to expelling them from the association, it will also request the government to severely punish them according to the law. Article 9: When members of the industry report smuggling, the association will not only strictly maintain secrecy, but also request the government to reward them according to the law. Article 10: Each group shall report the matters handled in these rules to the association on a daily list. Article 11: The association shall report the matters handled to the Private Inspection Committee of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce on a weekly basis for reference. Article 12: These rules shall be implemented after being approved by this committee and reported to the competent authorities and the Private Inspection Committee of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce for approval. The same shall apply to modifications.

Interception at the Intersection of Route Paul Henry · Seven Sacks of Narcotics Seized · Weighing Three Hundred and Forty-Four Pounds · Car Driver Chen Huqiu of Tongzhou Arrested

At No. 23 Daqing Lane, Yunnan Road, someone had established the Tongxing Company to supply and manufacture raw materials for the narcotic pill "Red Pill." The transportation of goods was highly secretive. At 9:10 AM the previous morning, Chen Huqiu, a car driver from Tongzhou, was hired to transport seven sacks of powdered sugar, saccharin, and coffee essence, weighing three hundred and forty-four pounds. He was traveling along Route Paul Henry, intending to deliver them to a certain organization in Caojiadu, when he was intercepted by Chinese detectives Liu Junjie and Liu Shuxun, etc., from the Avenue Haig police station, who found his behavior suspicious. They immediately stopped him and questioned him, learning the whole story. They then rushed to the company, where they apprehended Liu Xingfu, a native of Ningbo. The main culprit escaped during the chaos. In the rear wing, they found a large quantity of raw materials: powdered white, 148 pounds plus 88 pounds, including the barrels; charcoal, 43 pounds including the barrel; one package of Angelica dahurica root, weighing half a pound; cinchona salt powder, weighing seven pounds including the can; resin, weighing twenty-three pounds including the can; coffee essence, weighing five pounds including the can; one package of white resin, weighing half a pound; and seven account books. All were taken to the police station. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Third Criminal Tribunal of the First Special District Court. Attorney Zhang Shizhu of the Public Works Department explained the situation and requested a postponement to analyze the aforementioned materials. Subsequently, Chinese and Western detectives reported the details of the arrest, and the raw materials for the narcotic pill "Red Pill" were presented for inspection. The car driver Chen Huqiu testified that a stranger near the company on Second Avenue hired him to transport the seven sacks of materials to Caojiadu. The stranger escaped during the arrest, and he knew nothing else, pleading for leniency. Liu Xingfu testified that the company was established on February 2nd of this year and that a customer surnamed Zhou came to purchase something that was not raw materials for the "Red Pill." He also hired Attorney Eson to defend him. Judge Zhong Qing ordered that they remain in custody for further investigation at a later date.

Yu Qiaqing Cables Zhenhai County, Thoroughly Investigating the Case of Unwarranted Detention of the Town Head

Yu Qiaqing, Chairman of the Ningbo Native Association, learned that the town head of Daqi in Zhenhai was arbitrarily detained by the local Public Security Bureau. Yesterday, he specifically sent a telegram to the Zhenhai County Magistrate requesting a thorough investigation. The text of the telegram reads: "Respectfully addressed to Zhang, County Magistrate of the Zhenhai County Government: It has come to our attention that Xu Yunqin, the town head of Gaotang Town in the Fifth District of Zhenhai, together with He Xiangsheng, the head of Wanghe Township; Yu Heyu, the head of Beima Township; Gu Chunian, the head of Yongfeng Township; Wang Xitang, the head of Yan Yi Township; Le Wuchen, the head of Yan Er Township; Yu Kunfeng, the head of Henghe Township; Wang Fucheng, the head of Bei Xin Township; Yu Baoxing, the head of Shiqiu Township; and citizens Lin Guoyu, Gu Weikui, Wang Yuxiong, and others, have jointly telegraphed, stating that Yu Meitang, the town head of Daqi Town in their district and concurrently the captain of the Second County Security Brigade, was summoned by the police of the Daqi Public Security Bureau, directed by Chief Lin Guangyuan, on the 16th night. The following day, he was sent to the Ningxian District Security Command and detained. More than three days have passed, and the truth remains unclear. We have repeatedly telegraphed the county government for legal relief, but have received orders that the matter was previously unknown. Now, Town Head Yu has been released on bail by the Command after interrogation on the 20th. It is said that the Public Security Bureau Chief flattered party members and acted recklessly. When the summons was issued, no official document was presented; instead, they claimed the case was serious and immediately imposed martial law, prohibiting telegrams. Ten policemen, escorted by party member Zhao Xun and a 'Committee Member Yang' from the provincial party headquarters (self-proclaimed), arbitrarily directed the escort, handing him over at Kongshuling to armed soldiers of some unknown organization in the middle of the night, who then transferred him to Zhao Xun's residence in Jiangnan Doutou for detention. At the same time, Gu Fugui and He Yinning, who were arrested with him, were subjected to coercive interrogation with rattan canes at the Jiangfu police station and then sent to the county party headquarters before being transferred to the Ningxian District Security Command for detention. After interrogation, it was learned that the case involved Gu Yousheng's opium case in the town. The Baozhang (local neighborhood watch) was not satisfied with the punishment and fabricated accusations that the town head had taken bribes and let him go. Since town heads are civil servants under the leadership and supervision of party and government organs, any suspicion of crime or denouncement should be handled by their direct superiors or transferred to the judiciary. We have never heard of party members being able to arrest them directly, let alone conduct court trials, custodial detentions in private residences, or transfer them beyond the local government's judicial organs to party headquarters in neighboring counties for detention. Furthermore, the Public Security Bureau is an organ directly under the county government. Except in cases of violating police regulations, the arrest of criminals must be reported to the county government. When Town Head Yu was summoned to the bureau this time, the claim was that the case was too serious to be announced. How could he then be handed over to party members with no subordinate relationship for private removal? The intentions behind this are deeply suspicious. Under the clear blue sky, those who administer local self-government are being subjected to such illegal and oppressive treatment. How can the small, remote people be protected in the future? Town heads and others are implementing self-government and obeying administrative orders. If they are accused of wrongdoing, they will all take Yu Town Head's case as a lesson and be in constant fear for their safety. If we tolerate this without intervention, how will human rights be maintained in the future? In addition to continuing to telegram the county government requesting a thorough investigation, we hereby earnestly request the Guild to investigate by telegram and swiftly provide assistance, separately requesting the provincial and county party and government organs to conduct a thorough investigation and provide clear instructions to resolve the suspicions of the people." It is noted that the town head and citizens previously telegraphed us, requesting assistance. After our association telegraphed the Post County Security Command on the [day omitted]th, requesting that they quickly investigate and release him, we received telegram No. 131 from the Inspection Office, stating: "To the Shanghai Ningbo Association: I have received your telegram. Yu Meitang, the town head of Daqi Town in Zhenhai, was sent to this command by the Zhenhai County Party Headquarters for interrogation regarding the case of bribing opium offender Gu Fugui. After interrogation, he was released on bail. The Zhenhai County Magistrate was ordered to investigate the details of the case and report back for verification. This is to inform you for reference." Our association believes that town heads are civil servants. If there is indeed suspicion of crime, and they are reported or denounced, the proper procedure would be for their direct superiors to detain and transfer them to judicial or military courts for interrogation. However, the handling of this case, as described in the telegram—direct arrest, custodial detention in private residences, coercive interrogation, etc.—if true, appears to be an abuse of power. Based on the foregoing, we hereby urgently telegram Your Honor, the County Magistrate, requesting a thorough investigation and correction to uphold the law and dispel the suspicions of the people. We earnestly hope and pray for this." Signed, Yu Qiaqing, Chairman of the Ningbo Native Association.

The Child Laborers Dismissed by Customs Invited the Press Yesterday, Hoping Customs Will Reverse Its Decision, or Else Issue Retirement Compensation

The child laborers in the Jianghai Customs export section, after six of them were dismissed by the authorities a few days ago, have been in a state of panic. They have united and requested that the authorities reverse their decision and reinstate them. Furthermore, at 2:00 PM yesterday, they invited the press to the New World Hotel (originally intending to use the Customs Staff Club in Xiangkang Lane on Route Paul Henry, but it was rejected, so they temporarily changed to the New World Hotel) to report on the situation. They stated that the Jianghai Customs child laborers were hired three years ago, with a monthly living allowance of sixteen yuan. When they joined the customs, there was no stipulation regarding a three-year term. Recently, the Jianghai Customs authorities have used the excuse of three years having expired and have decided to dismiss the first batch of 28 child laborers and recruit new laborers. This has caused a reaction from all the old child laborers. To maintain their livelihoods, they request strong assistance from all sectors and demand that the Customs authorities continue to employ them. Otherwise, they request that the authorities give them six months' retirement compensation to prepare for finding work to survive during the transition.

Tragedy of Fatal Accident Involving a Municipal Bus · One Person Killed on the Spot, One Woman Seriously Injured · Three Others Also Struck, but Injuries Are Minor

At around 4:00 PM yesterday, the No. 10013 repair vehicle of the Municipal Bus Management Office of the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau, driven by Li Denghai (age 19, driver's license No. 1493) from Shandong, was traveling south to north when it reached the entrance of Chongqing Lane, No. 372 Fangxie Road, in the Nanshi district. A rickshaw was pulling a passenger in front. Because the road was curved and the car was traveling at a relatively high speed, the driver, upon seeing it, immediately braked. He braked too hard, causing the brake lever to break, making it impossible to control the vehicle. The car then hit and overturned the rickshaw. A female passenger from Suzhou, Tang Bo, 28 years old, who had come to Shanghai from her hometown to visit relatives, suffered injuries to her head and legs and lost consciousness. After the Western District Fire Brigade received the news, they immediately dispatched an ambulance to take her to Shanghai Hospital for treatment, where her life is in danger. The rickshaw driver, feeling guilty, ran away without a trace. At the same time, Jin Puhe, a 30-year-old Huangyan native who lived at No. 13-14 Tai'an Street, Fangxie Road, and worked as a machine-knitting wool craftsman, was passing by on the sidewalk when he was also struck in the head. He died immediately due to the severity of his injuries. He left behind elderly parents, a frail wife, and young children, all in his hometown. The deceased was living in Shanghai with his uncle, Mingfa, who was also in the machine-knitting wool clothing business. They have reported the case to the bureau and are awaiting the inspection of the body by the local court today, requesting legal action. There were three others with minor injuries: Wu Zhiqing, the young owner of the Yanlingtang Traditional Chinese Medicine store at No. 367 Fangxie Road, who was sitting nearby enjoying the cool air, suffered an injury to his left arm, and his stool was also crushed; Zhang Fulin, a resident of No. 361 on the same road, suffered injuries to his hands and feet; and Zhang Fuchang, a 13-year-old boy from No. 13, Chongqing Lane, Manufacturing Bureau Road, suffered a head injury. They were also taken by ambulance to Shanghai Hospital for treatment and returned home after bandaging.

Money Shop Collapses After Two Months of Operation · Manager and Others Charged · Capital Claimed to Be 10,000 Yuan · Actual Amount Only 1,500 Yuan · The Owner of a Metal Shop Files a Fraud Charge

The Yifeng Money Shop in Yongji Lane, Jiangxi Road, was opened in May of this year, with Zhao Liting from Zhenjiang as the manager, Li Yiqing from Wuxi as the assistant manager, and Zhu Xiangxian as the errand runner. The declared capital was 10,000 yuan. However, after operating for just over two months, it collapsed. Feng Zhongfang, the owner of the Renchangtai Metal Shop at No. 376 Waitan Road, Wuxi, had used three promissory notes from the shop, totaling 1,300 yuan, to exchange for cash on the 7th of last month, thanks to the mediator Huang Zhensheng. Zhu Xiangxian also paid with two promissory notes totaling 900 yuan on the 15th of last month. Feng also had dealings with the shop, which owed Feng 624.7 yuan. After the shop collapsed, Feng discovered that the shop's capital, although claimed to be 10,000 yuan, was actually only 1,500 yuan. This amount was deposited in the China Industrial Bank, where Huang Zhensheng was employed. According to common practice, all the capital of a money shop should be deposited with the mediator, who then hands it over to the manager after the shop opens. Now, the shop's capital was nominally 10,000 yuan, but only 1,500 yuan was deposited with the mediator, which is clearly a joint fraud. Therefore, he hired lawyer Hu Yong to file a lawsuit against Zhao Liting, Li Yixiao, Zhu Xiangxian, Huang Zhensheng, and shareholder Shi Yunliang, requesting that they be charged with the crime of obtaining property by fraud under Article 339 of the Criminal Code. The First Special District Court accepted the case and opened the Fifth Criminal Court for a hearing yesterday afternoon, presided over by Judge Chuan Lin. Only Huang Zhensheng appeared in court, as the others could not be found. Huang stated that the full 10,000 yuan in capital had been paid at the time, and that he did not recognize the shareholders. Judge Chuan stated that further investigation was needed and adjourned the hearing to a later date.

Whispers of Gossip

Reached a Settlement with Madam Mei

Distributed According to Law

But was not mentioned at all in the family property distribution contract, which is very confusing. The plaintiff believes his actions violate Article 335, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law, and therefore has filed a lawsuit. Returned as Old Debts

Road Association Promotes Manufacturing of Tires and Exploration for Gasoline

The China National Road Construction Association yesterday formulated a plan to promote the manufacturing of automobile tires and the exploration for gasoline. The standing committee resolved to actively carry it out, and has already sent letters to relevant agencies, organizations, and automobile companies to discuss everything. This move is of great importance to the future of the national transportation industry. The original document is recorded as follows: China National Road Construction Association's Plan to Promote the Manufacture of Automobile Tires and Exploration for Gasoline. (In the summer of the tenth year of the Republic of China, the chairman of this association, Dr. Wang Rutang, deeply felt the inconvenience of domestic transportation, making it difficult for various undertakings to develop. He invited comrades in Shanghai to engage in road construction. For fifteen years, he has actively promoted this, and to this day, the total length of roads completed nationwide has reached more than 100,000 kilometers. Those under construction and planned are even more numerous, like bamboo shoots after the rain, difficult to count. The number of highways nationwide has increased sharply, and municipal administrations in various places are gradually improving. However, remote areas are still not universally covered, and continued efforts should be made to achieve satisfactory results. Therefore, the National Economic Committee and the construction departments of various provinces are all working hard on this. We firmly believe that the road construction movement can win the promotion of the whole people. In the near future, the results will certainly meet our hopes. The road construction movement has a hopeful period of success. We should also work together on the following movements: (1) The movement to manufacture automobiles; (2) The movement to manufacture automobile tires; (3) The movement to explore for gasoline. We believe that the above three movements are extremely important at present. In recent years, the business of highway bureaus in various provinces and long-distance automobile companies, the national income, and the profits obtained by private investors have been considerable. The hard work of the authorities and organizers is deeply admirable. However, due to the development of this type of business, the consumption of automobile tires and gasoline has increased accordingly, and this consumption is entirely dependent on imports. The Chinese people are working hard on the highway business, but as a result, most of the income is indirectly sent to foreign capitalists. Thinking of this, we are deeply saddened. The parties concerned are more eager than anyone else to reverse the outflow of national interests and money. This can be asserted. This association plans to invite representatives from the construction departments of various provinces, the highway bureaus of various provinces, and long-distance automobile companies, as well as industrialists, capitalists, and social activists, to jointly discuss concrete measures, and to invite the National Economic Commission to jointly preside over them. This association's proposals for the above three movements are as follows: (1) Regarding the first and second movements, it is hoped that the National Economic Committee, the provincial and municipal governments, the long-distance automobile companies, the industrialists, and the capitalists will subscribe shares separately, gather capital, and set up factories to manufacture; (2) Gather specialized talents and pay more attention to recruiting Chinese talents trained by the British Ford Motor Company to manufacture automobiles; (3) Request the government to subsidize individuals or organizations to explore for oil, and request the government to specify reward measures. Whether individuals or organizations can find oil fields, the government or the people will be given special rights in the future to exploit them, as an incentive. This movement is of great importance to national rights, social economy, and it is hoped that all parties will give detailed instructions and propose measures, so as to request the Resources Committee of the National Economic Commission to jointly convene a meeting to discuss everything, so as to achieve the goal of cooperation between the people and the government, and to see the effectiveness of the people's political ability.
