Next, Zhou Renmao, the father of the deceased, stated that his daughter originally lived in Nanjing with her husband, and came to Shanghai in April to study obstetrics at the Ximen Hospital. On August 16th, she asked her mother to go and see her, saying that she had a fever and chills, so she was sent to Guangren Hospital. Dr. Zhang diagnosed that it was caused by an abortion and that the treatment was ineffective, resulting in death. He requested that the defendant be severely punished. Finally, the defendant's defense lawyer, Fan Gang, supplemented his opinion, stating that the deceased arrived at the defendant's place by rickshaw No. 3710 at 9:00 PM on August 16th, requesting treatment. The rickshaw cushion was already stained with blood. Whether the abortion was performed by the defendant is a question. He requested that rickshaw driver Zhou Zhilin be summoned to court for questioning. The court verified the confessions and, because the case still needed to be investigated and evidence examined, postponed the hearing to the morning of September 9th. The defendant was returned to custody.

Bleeding for Election: Wang Guansheng's Back of Head Chopped, Foot Bone Broken; Fight Over a Seat on the Tofu Guild Board

Wang Guansheng, owner of the Wang Shunxing tofu shop on Jiangyin Street, Xiaoximen, had a feud with his colleagues during the election of the board of directors a few days ago. Unexpectedly, during lunch a few days ago, a thug suddenly chopped Wang Guansheng on the back of the head with an axe, causing serious injuries and breaking his foot bone. He was sent to Qu Zhibu Hospital for treatment. Wang then filed a complaint with the police station, stating that Xu Haitao, a fellow tofu maker, wanted to seize the seat on the Tofu Guild Board and resorted to such a vicious act. The police station is investigating the matter. Xu Haitao went to the Qiaojiazha Tofu Guild for a meeting a few days ago, which Wang's wife learned about and rushed to arrest Xu and hand him over to the Xundao Street Police Station, who transferred him to the Wenmiao Road Police Station for investigation.

Suspects in the Qidong Murder and Arson Case Extradited from Shanghai Yesterday: Two Suspects Confess to Robbery and Murder; Court Approves Extradition to Qidong

In May of this year, a large group of bandits in Meijia Town, Qidong County, armed with weapons, invaded, murdered, and set fires. At that time, the residence of Shen, the village chief of the first district of the town, was burned by the bandits, and the homes of residents Song Tianwu and Bao Zhang Xu Ziyuan were also robbed by these people, who fled with the stolen goods. After a secret investigation by Xu Hongfu of the Qidong County Government, it was discovered that two key suspects in the case, Dai A'gang and Xu Renchang (also known as Xu Shishi), had fled and were hiding at No. 20 Doupai, 234 Lane, Mabai Road, Shanghai Public Concession. So he came to Shanghai a few days ago, reported it to the Municipal Public Security Bureau, who reported it to the Putuo Road Police Station, who assisted the Chinese and Western detectives in arresting Dai and Xu and detaining them in the First Special Court for interrogation. Yesterday morning, the date for the continued interrogation had arrived, and Qidong County had also prepared official documents and sent detective Xu Hongfu and eyewitness Huang A'gen to the court, requesting extradition. Huang A'gen confessed that he was from Qidong, 31 years old, and proved that Dai and Xu were indeed involved in the robbery and murder case. Zhang Tianyin, the police station lawyer, agreed to the extradition. Judge Huang Risheng ordered Dai and Xu to be handed over to the officials from the Qidong County Government to be taken back to Qidong for further investigation.

Lao Zha Police Station Captures Many Thieves, Seizes Guns and Bullets, Detains Suspects for Investigation of Cases and Further Interrogation

Li Shugui, a Chinese detective of the Lao Zha Police Station, and detectives Xue Youwen and Ding Yizhong, learned that many thieves were hiding at No. 376 Maite Hersh's Road, so they secretly went to arrest them at 8:30 AM the day before yesterday. They arrested Wang Shaokang (also known as Xiao Wu) and Ding Youjin (also known as Chen Hanzhang), both from Anhui, on the spot. They found a Lianqian pistol and a bullet on Wang, as well as two automatic pistol bullets. They were taken back to the police station, and they confessed that the pistol was supplied by Zhao Chenquan (also known as Zhao Lao San), who lived at No. 211, Lane 679, Xiaoshadu Road, for use in committing crimes. So they went and arrested Zhao. Then, Detective Li and others received a tip-off and continued to capture Fang Fabiao and Shi Yucheng, both from Anhui, near Xiaoshadu Road. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the First Criminal Court of the First Special District. Police Station Lawyer Wang Yaotang prosecuted Wang, Ding, and Zhao according to Article 1, Paragraph 1 of the Regulations on the Prohibition of Military Firearms, requesting a postponement to facilitate the investigation of the crimes they committed. As for Fang and Shi, they requested permission to be detained and claimed that the report obtained by the police station indicated that Fang and others were accomplices of Wang and others. However, after investigation, it was found that Fang and Shi may be related to the bombing case, and a postponement of the hearing was also requested. After Judge Feng Shide verified the report and briefly questioned Wang and others, he ordered the hearing to be postponed for another week.

Shanghai Opera Association Sues; Verdict on Sichuan Opera Special Issue; Lu Han Cheng and Others Not Guilty

Shi Chunxuan, a standing committee member of the Shanghai Shanghai Opera Research Association, No. 1 Fuchang Lane, Yunnan Road, Public Concession, represented the association and hired lawyer Zhou Lianze to file a lawsuit with the Criminal Court of the First Court against Yu Hancheng, the manager of the Sichuan Grand Stage, currently performing at the New Guangda Theater, and Sun Jiayu and Liu Zuoxiang (all from Sichuan), the editors of the Sichuan Opera Special Issue, alleging that the first issue of the Sichuan Opera Special Issue, published on August 5th, contained libelous statements against all members of the Shanghai Shanghai Opera Research Association, damaging their reputation, and requesting an investigation. The case was once heard by Judge Sun Pengxian, who announced the conclusion and scheduled a date for the verdict. All these circumstances have been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday, the date for the verdict arrived, and neither party was present. Judge Sun presided over the Second Criminal Court and ruled that Lu Hancheng, Sun Jiayu, and Liu Zuoxiang were all not guilty. It is reported that the plaintiff side is dissatisfied with this verdict and will file an appeal with the High Third Branch Court.

Tomb Robbing: Qin Zhuangyuan's Tomb Robbed; Jade Cup, Jade Bracelet, and Incense Burner Found; Dispute Over Unequal Distribution of Loot

A man named Huang Lao Si from Huanglou Township, Nanhui Third District, Pudong, has been doing business outside and has accumulated some wealth. He previously purchased a piece of land in the Thirty-Seventh District, which contained the Qin family tomb. A certain Jia from the township, after learning that the Qin family had produced a Zhuangyuan (top scholar) in the past and that there must be valuable items in the tomb, hired a professional tomb raider, Zhou, to open the tomb at night. He obtained valuable items such as a pair of jade cups and jade bracelets. Zhou stole a gold incense burner and sold it to a pawnshop. Jia learned of this and went to negotiate, demanding that Zhou hand over the gold incense burner. The Qin family has now learned of this and is pursuing the matter.

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:00 PM yesterday stated that the sky is cloudy around Shandong, with strong northeast winds. The sky is cloudy in the lower reaches of the Yangtze River, with a possibility of showers and strong southeast winds. There are strong cyclones around the East China Sea and Taiwan, with bad weather, due to the hurricane south of the Ryukyu Islands moving northwest. The center of the hurricane was within 120 miles of 23 degrees north latitude and 118 degrees east longitude at noon. The wind strength is unknown. September 2nd

Announcing the Adjustment of the Chinese Buddhist Association to All Monks and Nuns in the Country

— Zhang Tinghao

The Chinese Buddhist Association, from its inception to the present, although it has some history, its organization has never been sound, and most monks and nuns have not joined. Of course, there may be one or two monks and nuns with both wisdom and virtue who are unwilling to join for the sake of personal practice. However, because the organization and facilities of the association have not fully satisfied people's expectations, it is feared that not a few are unwilling to join. Perhaps there are still some monks and nuns who simply do not know that there is a Chinese Buddhist Association, let alone join it. The small number of monks involved in the association's affairs are rarely able to adhere to the Buddhist teachings of "no self, no dispute." Most are stubbornly attached to their own ego, and because of differences in thought and opinion, they secretly divide into new and old factions, each supporting their leaders and vying for leadership. Therefore, the more knowledgeable Yuan Ying and Tai Xu have become objects of support for these monks and nuns. Thus, outsiders believe that the dispute within the Chinese Buddhist Association is the dispute between Yuan Ying and Tai Xu, which is truly, Amitabha. Although there are many factions among monks and nuns across the country, I think that if the leaders of these two major factions can truly lead by example, dissolve their prejudices, adhere to the Buddhist teachings of "no self, no contention," and cooperate sincerely, the dispute within the Chinese Buddhist Association could be at least halved. If the dispute is not resolved, the unity will not be strong. If the unity is not strong, the affairs of the association will naturally be unable to be promoted. Since the dispute within the Buddhist Association is largely related to Yuan Ying and Tai Xu, Yuan Ying and Tai Xu cannot shirk their responsibility for the past failure of the Buddhist Association's affairs to be promoted smoothly. Thus, whether the Buddhist Association can "unite all monks and nuns in the country, regulate the precepts, propagate the teachings, promote the spirit of Mahayana salvation, benefit the people, and benefit society," and fulfill the mission of promoting the Dharma and benefiting the world, although monks and nuns in general should work together, Yuan Ying and Tai Xu should unite sincerely and set an example for monks and nuns across the country, ensuring that the group of Shakyans with no self and no dispute will no longer have disputes, so that they will not be ashamed of being Buddhist disciples and leaders of the community.

I was ordered to adjust the Chinese Buddhist Association and spent several months of investigation and research to see the source of the diseases of the Chinese Buddhist Association and the general abbots and monks. The source of the disease of the Buddhist Association has been explained in the previous section. The source of the disease of the general abbots and monks lies in abandoning the inherent duty of promoting the Dharma and benefiting the world. The abbots regard the temple monks and religious property as private property, and devote themselves to maintaining religious property as their only task. The rest of the monks and nuns regard performing Buddhist rituals for patrons as a profession, thinking that attending Buddhist rituals is fulfilling the responsibility that should be fulfilled as a monk. They do not understand the scriptures, do not observe the precepts, no wonder the lion worms increase day by day, the monks' virtues decline day by day, and the teachings decline day by day.

I cannot bear the name without substance of the Chinese Buddhist Association, and the increasing degradation of the personality of monks and nuns, so I decided to draft seventy articles to revise the draft of the Chinese Buddhist Association's charter for the Buddhist Association, and attach an explanation. With the approval of the Minister, I, in my capacity as the director of the competent authority, first handed over the draft charter to the current chairman of the association, the monk Yuan Ying, to be forwarded to all directors and supervisors and monks and nuns in various places for thorough study, and to express their opinions as much as possible. The intention is nothing more than to urge monks and nuns across the country to pay attention to the Chinese Buddhist Association, to pool their efforts, and to achieve the purpose of enlightening others and benefiting others from self-awareness, self-help, and self-government. The draft charter could have been submitted to the Minister for approval and ordered the Chinese Buddhist Association to comply with it by ministerial order, because I hope that monks and nuns across the country will understand the intention of the central government to adjust the Chinese Buddhist Association, so as not to be incited by one or two reckless people, and at the same time, to give them the opportunity to participate in the discussion and contribute their opinions on the draft charter, which is related to their own interests. And by this, it can also test whether Chinese Buddhists have a real understanding and belief in Buddhism, so the draft charter was first handed over to the monk Yuan Ying to be forwarded to the monks and nuns for public study. This is my motivation and sincerity for drafting the charter for the Chinese Buddhist Association. The draft charter is certainly not perfect, and there may be some provisions that should be revised or supplemented, but compared with the current charter of the association, I dare say that it is much more complete. In the past few weeks, I have received opinions from monks and nuns in various places on the draft charter, and the texts seen in the newspapers have mostly expressed agreement. However, recently, news has come from friends in Shanghai that a few monks and laymen seem to have doubts about the four points in the draft charter, and I will explain them separately later. (To be continued)

This Year's Second Quarter Shanghai Industrial and Commercial Activity Report (Continued) (Thirty-five General Industrial and Commercial Conditions in Shanghai)

— Edited by China Credit Investigation

B. Important Industrial and Commercial House Changes in May

A. In Special Businesses

A. Financial Industry Category

1. Reopening of the Shanghai Branch of the Hong Kong National Bank: After the Hong Kong head office of the bank telegraphed on September 16th of last year ordering the closure of the business, eight months have passed. This time, after the creditors and shareholders discussed and decided to reopen according to the agreement between the two parties. The Hong Kong head office opened on March 2nd, and the Shanghai branch continued operations on the 1st of this month. Ma Huibi was re-elected as manager, and 600,000 yuan of new shares were raised. Creditors with deposits of more than 100 yuan will use half of the amount as shares and half will be repaid in ten installments.

2. Expansion of the Italian Commercial Bank of Italy: Recently, in order to develop its business and seek closer ties with Chinese merchants, the bank has increased its total capital to 2 million Italian lire and hired financial experts Kang Zhiyin and Wu Guoying as Chinese managers to specialize in all banking business and credit lending.

3. New establishment of the Shanghai Citizens' Accumulation Loan Bank: The headquarters of the company is located in Japan, specializing in savings and loan business, and emphasizing small loans; recently, in order to expand its scope, a branch has been established in Shanghai, managed by Lei Midi Si, which announced its opening on the 12th of this month.

B. Restaurants: In the middle of this month, two long-established restaurants declared liquidation: one is the Pin Fang Cantonese Restaurant at 459 Dong Wuchang Road. The building has been in business for nearly 20 years. Recently, due to the sluggish market and poor business, it declared liquidation and invited bids. The second is the Hong Yun Restaurant at 90 Fujian Road, which has also been open for decades, but recently it has also been said that the business is not good and the turnover is not flexible, and finally it is impossible to maintain. However, the restaurant was taken over and reopened by Chu Rulin and others on the 28th.

B. In Manufacturing Industry

1. Liquidation of Yiyuan Rubber Manufacturing Factory: The factory was first established in Hong Kong. Since moving to Shanghai, it has been in business for more than ten years. The actual capital is 100,000 yuan, with Yang Mingsheng as manager. It employs 150 or 60 workers and can produce 2,400 pairs of sneakers per day. At the beginning of its establishment, the business was still developing. In the past three years, due to the dumping of foreign goods and the sharp drop in prices, the annual loss has reached 560,000 yuan. It has been delayed until now, and finally it has declared that it cannot be maintained due to inflexible turnover.

2. The Central Sanyong Light Bulb Factory and the Qite Free Light Bulb Factory opened: Both factories aim to manufacture multi-filament light bulbs. The former was established by Chen Weizhou with sole investment, with a capital of 50,000 yuan. The latter was founded by Bao Yimin and Yu Weiqing.

C. In Sales and Commercial Industry

1. Establishment of Shanghai Branch of Xingzhong Company: The company is an economic institution of Japan to China, and has close relationship with the government and Mitsui, Mitsubishi and other consortia. The head office held its founding meeting at the Dasu Mantetsu Kaisha on December 20th of last year, with a capital of 10 million Japanese yen, divided into 200,000 shares, all of which were received by Mantetsu. The president is Togawa Shinji. In addition to Shanghai, branches are planned to be established in Tianjin, Guangdong, Tokyo, Osaka and other places with the same organization. The manager of the Shanghai branch is Miyazaki Masuhira; specializing in cotton, yarn, steel materials, etc., in order to achieve the so-called economic cooperation between China and Japan. The establishment and future development of the company are worthy of attention. (To be continued)

Our World Games Football Team Loses Again to the English Amateur Cup Champion: Defeated 2-5 by Casuals, Leading 2-1 Before Conceding Four Consecutive Goals, Technique and Cooperation Above the English Team

London, September 1st, Reuters: The Chinese World Games football team, after losing 2-3 to Corinthians yesterday, lost 2-5 to Casuals today. Casuals are the champions of last season's amateur cup. The match was held at the Crystal Palace ground in Selhurst Park.

Since yesterday's experience, the Chinese team was very locked in during the first half today, preserving their strength. Until five minutes before the end of the first half, they were still able to compete with the English team.

The Chinese team's technique and cooperation are very good, indeed above the runners-up of the Isthmian League. But the English team's Jones was indeed a major obstacle for the Chinese team.

Corinthians, the champion of this amateur cup, scored first. Li Huitang also broke the enemy's goal before the end of the first half, making it a tie.

At the beginning of the second half, the Chinese team took the lead again. Sun Jinshun scored another goal in a very moving posture. Casuals were not afraid at all and counterattacked fiercely, with a very beautiful performance, the audience, in one breath, scored four consecutive goals, winning 5-2.

Le Ray scored a tie from very close range. Allen made it 3-2. Neal and Jones dribbled in near the end of the game and each scored another goal.

Owens Has Become a Professional Athlete: Accepts a Reward of $5,000 a Week, Will Go to Various Places to Perform or Appear on Stage

Havas News Agency, New York, 1st: Black athlete Owens, who participated in the 11th Olympic Games in Berlin last month and won the 100 meters, 200 meters, and long jump championships, has returned with honor. He suddenly joined the professional athlete team and is said to have accepted a reward of $5,000 a week. He joined the professional track and field team and will travel with Turun, the champion of the 100 meters at the 10th Olympic Games (also a black man), to perform for ten weeks, and then go to Australia and Japan to perform.

New York, September 1st, Reuters: The world-renowned black athlete Owens has turned professional. Owens has signed a contract with a theater performance host to perform professional races or appear on stage.

Owens's Biography

Owens, this year's Berlin World Games, won the 100 meters, 200 meters, and long jump championships. He will be 22 years old on the 12th of this month (September). He has seven siblings. When he was four years old, the whole family moved to Cleveland, Ohio. A few years later, when he was studying at Fairmont Junior High School, he was playing games with children in front of the school. Coach Charles Riley's swift pace made a deep impression on Owens. Riley asked Owens why he didn't make considerable efforts in track and field. Owens's legs had developed beyond his age. After Owens and Riley negotiated with his family for a long time, they agreed to start practicing track and field.

High School Life

Soon after his amazing track and field life began, Owens did not forget Riley's cultivation, and immediately gave Riley a watch won in a university intercollegiate competition. In high school, Owens created three national secondary school records. Not long ago, after Owens created a record of 9.4 seconds, twenty-eight universities and colleges persuaded him to transfer. When Owens was preparing to enter university, these universities became one of his learning schools.

University Life

Owens entered Ohio State University. His sophomore year was his first year as a university athlete. He participated in the Nine University Games and Owens scored a total of 115 points, twenty-one firsts, two seconds, and two thirds. During his university studies, Owens read while working, and worked as a gas station attendant in his spare time. Owens is similar to the heavyweight boxing champion Louis of the sensational state of Georgia. Not only did he study and work, but he also used his savings to support his family, sending a portion of his income to his family in Cleveland every week.

Since the opening of the games, it has been windy and rainy every day. It was not until the sixth day that the weather was clear. I don't know why they both failed to jump in the trial, so they were not qualified to participate in the preliminaries. However, of the 37 athletes who participated, only 23 qualified. The preliminary round was held at 4:30 pm. Each person jumped three times. Japanese athlete Tajima Naoto jumped 15.76 meters in the first jump, breaking the Games record (the Games record was 15.72 meters set by Japanese Nambu Chuhei in 1932), and ranked first. The second jump was out of bounds, and the third jump was also 15.44 meters. The world record (15.78 meters set in 1935) holder, Australian Metcalfe, scored 15.50 meters in the first jump, the second jump was out of bounds, and the third jump was 14.67 meters, ranking second. The third was Japanese athlete Harada Masao, with a jump of 15.39 meters, a second jump of 15.45 meters, and a third jump of 15.42 meters. The fourth was German athlete Warner, with a first jump of 15.37 meters, and the second and third jumps were out of bounds. The fifth was Japanese athlete Oshima Kamakichi, with a first jump of 15.07 meters, and the second and third jumps were also out of bounds. The sixth was American athlete Romano, with a first jump of 14.68 meters, a second jump out of bounds, and a third jump of 14.90 meters. The two Japanese athletes were both listed among the six finalists, and their momentum was extremely strong. The finals were held immediately. Romano jumped first, the first jump was out of bounds, the second jump was 15.08 meters, just surpassing Japanese athlete Oshima, and the third jump slightly regressed to 15.04 meters. Oshima's first jump was out of bounds, and his ranking dropped to sixth. Warner's first jump was 14.53 meters, the second jump was out of bounds, and the third jump was 14.23 meters, with no progress, and remained in fourth place. Harada's first jump was 15.50 meters, already tied with Metcalfe, the second jump regressed to 15.27 meters, and the third jump advanced to 15.66 meters, surpassing Metcalfe, while Metcalfe's three jumps, the first jump was only 14.83 meters, the second jump was out of bounds, and the third jump was only 15.20 meters, and retreated to third. The veterans in this competition were generally depressed, in other words, the strength of the newcomers is terrifying. Japanese Tajima's results in the preliminary round were already firmly ranked first, but in the first jump of the finals, he achieved a score of 16 meters, breaking the world record, which is as valuable as Owens' long jump. The second jump was 15.65 meters, and the third jump was out of bounds. The complete results are as follows:

Life of the World Games Inspection Group - Sent by Jiang Zhende from Berlin on July 16th

Berlin Correspondence: After arriving in Germany, the World Games Inspection Group and the national athlete group stayed in separate locations. The athlete group stayed in the Olympic Village, while the Inspection Group stayed in the International Sports Academy Camp. The entire experience was like military camp life, eating hard bread and drinking ice water. Initially, it was unfamiliar, but gradually we grew accustomed to it. About thirty countries, with approximately twenty-eight people from each country, participated in the event, gathering together cheerfully. Each day, different countries took turns performing, and famous figures gave speeches. Since the opening of the Games, we have been visiting daily. After the Games, we will travel to various places for inspection. The entire group is scheduled to leave Europe with the athlete group on September 3rd and return to China. The inspection schedule and a list of camp life are provided below to show a glimpse of our daily routine while carrying out this mission.

Camp Life

July 24th: Opening ceremony held at the camp in the morning. Immediately followed by a review and a meeting. In the afternoon at 3:00 PM, guided tour of the entire venue.

25th: At 4:00 PM, Dr. Jack from Germany gives a lecture, and Dr. Kromelan gives a speech. At 5:30 PM, Professor Steenhaus from the United States gives a lecture.

26th: At 2:00 PM, camp members take a steamboat tour of Hafen Lake and cross Stoßensee-Süd.

27th: At 11:00 AM, formation performance of German-style gymnastics. At 4:00 PM, a leader of German sports gives a lecture. At 5:00 PM, Dr. Stöscheck gives a lecture. At 8:30 PM, Xi Nao-style dance performance at the camp.

28th: At 8:00 AM, performance of British and Canadian-style gymnastics at the camp. At 10:00 AM, performance of children's exercises. At 11:00 AM, Secretary-General Dr. Ding from Germany gives a lecture. At 3:00 PM, visit to the cultural and art exhibition, and lectures by Major Neumann and Dr. Stock from Germany. At 4:00 PM, formation performance of German-style gymnastics.

29th: At 8:30 AM, performance of Italian-style formation splitting. At 11:00 AM, performance of Dutch-style formation, and practice of flexibility exercises according to the Dutch natural air breathing method. At 4:00 PM, Camp Commander Challing (Swedish) gives a lecture. At 5:30 PM, Inspector Knudson gives a lecture.

30th: At 9:30 AM, Czech-style performance. At 10:30 AM, Finnish-style performance. At 4:00 PM, Dr. Leikola from Finland gives a lecture. At 5:00 PM, Professor Kleber from Germany demonstrates various formation methods. At 5:30 PM, Professor Changqu from Germany gives a lecture.

31st: At 9:00 AM, Professor Nashee from the United States gives a lecture. At 10:00 AM, Meichou provides guidance on nursing methods. At 2:00 PM, various aerial stunt performances (World Championship finals). At 8:30 PM, a banquet for all camp members (Guoguang Society).

City Sports Meet - Preparatory Meeting - Addition of Chinese Martial Arts to Competitions

The fourth City Sports Meet, organized by the City Education Bureau, is scheduled to be held from October 22nd to 24th at the stadium in the city center. The preparatory committee held a preparatory meeting yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM at the City Education Bureau. Committee members present included Chen Gongshou (representing Zhang), Jiang Jianbai, Mi Jifang, Ma Chonggan, Shao Rugan (representing Wang), Zhang Yongchun, Wang Keyong, Li Jiyuan, Wang Fudan, and others. Chairman Jiang Jianbai conducted a detailed discussion of the draft rules for the sports meet, which will be announced after submission to the City Government for record-keeping. The main points are recorded below:

Eligibility for Each Group

This year's meet is divided into four groups: Open, University, Middle School, and Physical Education School. The Open group is based on individual participation, while the other groups are based on school participation. The eligibility requirements are as follows: For the Open group, any citizen within the city limits, male aged 18 or older, female aged 16 or older, with sound health, good character, and not violating the qualifications and spirit of amateur sports, may participate. The remaining groups consist of students currently enrolled in the respective schools, with schools as the units of participation. The Middle School group is divided into senior and junior high school sections, and the Physical Education School group is divided into specialized and normal school sections. Physical education colleges participate in the Physical Education School group and do not participate in the University group.

Organization of the Congress

It is reported that the Mayor will serve as Honorary President, the Director of the Education Bureau as President, two supervising section chiefs as Vice Presidents, and the Physical Education Supervisor as Secretary-General. The organization is divided into two departments: Administrative and Competitive. Each department has one director. The Administrative Department includes six sections: Documentation, Accounting, General Affairs, Reception, Security, and Hygiene. The Competitive Department includes nine sections: Venue and Equipment, Registration and Allocation, Refereeing, Recording, and Awards. There is also a Qualification Review Committee to review the qualifications of athletes, and a Judging Committee to adjudicate all sports-related disputes during the event. Personnel for each position will be appointed by the Director of the Education Bureau.

Addition of Chinese Martial Arts

The meet originally planned to have two sections: Group Exercises and Track and Field. Now, at the request of the City Martial Arts Hall, a Chinese Martial Arts section has been added, with individual participation. It is divided into performance and competition groups. The performance group is divided into male and female boxing and weapons. The competition group is divided into wrestling, archery (Chinese), slingshot, and weightlifting, with male and female groups. The track and field events are generally the same as those announced previously. It is proposed to change the number of places awarded to four for each event.

Trial Organization of Group Competitions by University Sports Associations - Cross-Country Race in the First Semester - Tug-of-War in the Second Semester

Since the reorganization of the Jiangnan University Sports Association, the Shanghai University Sports Association has been established, with Jhih Tze University, Great China University, Guanghua University, and Fudan University serving as executive committee members. Rong Qizhao is the chairman, and Wang Fudan is the vice-chairman. After Mr. Rong left the country with the World Games delegation, Wang Fudan has been in charge of the association's affairs. This Shanghai News reporter met with Mr. Wang yesterday, who said that the executive committee members Rong Qizhao, Chen Bingde, and Peng Wenyu convened a meeting on the Mediterranean Sea, one day before arriving in Venice, to decide on the progress of the association's affairs. The records are being sent now. A selection is provided below:

Amendment of Rules - Executive Committee Chairman Rong Qizhao, Recorder Peng Wenyu, Resolutions: Wang Fudan is appointed as the permanent chairman of the Tennis Championship Committee. Official notification is sent to the university authorities, requesting them to participate in the association as formal members. Based on the Jiangnan University constitution, the following rules are amended: Each school member must participate in at least one sport organized by the association each semester. Each school must pay membership dues of 20 yuan per academic year, and a registration fee of 5 yuan for each sport participated in. Anyone who has graduated from any university and obtained a degree may not participate in championship competitions.

Pilot Competitions - Regarding the trial organization of group competitions, it was decided to hold a cross-country race in the first semester, with at least 100 participants (excluding those who have represented their schools in competitions organized by the association). The date is the last Saturday of December this year at 3:00 PM. The route will be at most two miles, and the location will be decided later. A tug-of-war will be held in the second semester, with 100 participants (divided into five groups: A, B, C, D, and E, with 20 people per school per group). Each group pulls three times, with one point awarded to the winner each time. The group with the highest total score for the five groups wins. The competition method will be a knockout system. The date is the last Saturday of April at 3:00 PM, and the location will be decided later. Group A of each group will compete against each other.

Jiangsu Province to Pilot Guidance Zone System

The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education has specially formulated a "Method for Implementing the Elementary Education Guidance Zone System on a Trial Basis in Jiangsu Province" to pilot the elementary education guidance zone system. It is reported that it will be implemented soon. The method stipulates that each normal school district in the province will consist of 20 to 30 elementary schools as a guidance zone. The provincial supervisor inspecting the district will appoint an elementary education instructor, and the educational bureau director, county supervisor, educational committee members, normal school principal, and affiliated elementary school principal will organize a guidance zone committee, with the elementary education instructor as the guidance counselor. The guidance counselor will be permanently stationed in the district, actively guiding each school in the district, and assessing their progress. When necessary, demonstration teaching, mutual visits, critiques, and exhibitions/competitions will be held to facilitate mutual learning. When existing supervisors inspect the district, they should also be guided by the guidance counselor. If administrative sanctions are needed, the consent of the guidance counselor should be obtained. The method also stipulates that the guidance counselor should submit the diagnostic inspection guidance plan and process to the provincial supervisor for review and submission to the Education Department for approval and public announcement, to serve as a reference for education administrative personnel and elementary school teachers in each county.

Finance: Pure Gold Slightly Declines... Many Investors Selling Off - Gold Auction Results Decline by Six Jiao

Gold Market: Yesterday, pure gold slightly declined. The market opened with a slight downturn, fluctuating by about four jiao in the morning. The middle of the day was uneventful, and the final result was a decline of six jiao. At the start of the morning, overseas silver market news showed London rising and the U.S. unchanged. Speculation among large brokerage houses suggested that some Indian traders were selling after the market closed. Montri futures silver prices rose by between 2.2 and 3.5 cents, with exchange rates increasing. London spot gold fell by half a penny. The Central Bank's official exchange rates were announced, with both the British and American rates unchanged. Customs gold unit remained unchanged. The official standard gold auction price was announced as 1123.9 yuan. Trading outside the market was slightly weak. The market opened lower, and due to some panic among long position holders, the price declined. Spot buyers encouraged activity when prices fell, managing to maintain the market. HSBC's official exchange rates were announced, with both the British and American rates unchanged, and the silver balancing tax rose by half a cent. After this, prices gradually improved, but many small investors took advantage of the high prices to sell, resulting in a flat situation at noon. The half-day market situation is recorded below:

The market opened at 1128 yuan, down three jiao from the previous closing. Dingkang, Hengyu, Jingfu sold off, retreating to 7.6 yuan. Dadecheng, Fuxing, Yongshengyuan, Yong purchased bars. HSBC's official exchange rates were announced, with both the British and American rates unchanged, and the silver balancing tax was announced to rise by half a cent, with little impact. Qian Changxiang and Dachangxiang also bought, rising to 8 yuan. Dadecheng, Dacheng, and Tongtaichang sold off. The market closed at noon at 1127.7 yuan.

The closing price was the Central Bank's official standard gold auction price of 1123.9 yuan. Relative to the closing price, it was approximately 4 yuan lower. Logged transactions for the current month were at 1125 yuan, and for October at 1128 yuan. Morning water compensation was at 1125 yuan. The spot market situation was uneventful. Tianjin goods were quoted at an additional 13 yuan, and "sha chi" price was quoted at an additional 11 yuan. Selling price was quoted at an additional 14.5 yuan, with little trading. Swaps were also calm.

Trading within the market was limited. Overall, Shengyuan, Yongfutai, Hengfutai, Yongdadecheng, etc., were on the buying side, while Tongtaichang, Lifeng, Shenda, Yongdingkang, Yuanmao, Yongdacheng, etc., were on the selling side.

The half-day market situation was extremely stable. The market opened at 1128 yuan, and closed at noon at 1127.7 yuan. The highest was 1128 yuan, and the lowest was 1127.6 yuan, with only four jiao of fluctuation. The total number of transactions for the half-day was 749 bars.

Of the bar transactions for the current month that have not yet been settled, the long position holders include Futaiheng with over 200 bars, and Qingfayong and Qiafengyong with over 100 each. The short position holders include Jingfu with over 400 bars, and Yicheng with over 100 bars. The total number of remaining transactions is 672 bars, with 9 long position holders and 5 short position holders.

The lineup for October positions includes: Long position holders include Qiafengyong with over 1,700, Fuxingyong and Hengchangyong with over 800 each, Dachangxiang with over 900, Wanxing with over 700, Shenkang, Dingkang, and Wuchangxiang with over 400 each, Shunlifuda, Yuanmaoyong, and Huixiang with over 200 each, and Qingfayong, Dashenyuan, Hengfu, Yu, etc., with over 100 each. US Exchange Rates Show Slight Loosening

Exchange Market: Yesterday, the British and American exchange rates rose, causing the US exchange rate to show slight loosening. The majority of the transactions during the half-day were swaps, and the overall trend was very sluggish. At the start of the morning, overseas telegrams showed that London's near and far rates both rose by 1.25, with brokerage houses saying that speculators were selling after the market closed and that a few Indian traders were buying. The New York silver market was unchanged, and Montri futures silver prices rose by between 1.2 and 3.5 cents. London spot gold fell by half a penny. The British-American rate rose by 1.25, the British-French rate rose by 2 pounds, the American-British rate rose by 0.1875, and the American-French rate fell by 0.0625. The Central Bank's official exchange rates were announced, with both the British and American rates unchanged. The Customs gold unit remained unchanged. The exchange market opened with the selling price for the near-term British exchange rate at 1 shilling, 2 pence, 0.375 and 0.40625 pairing, and the US exchange rate at 30.1875 yuan, which was unchanged for the British and down 0.03125 for the US compared to the previous closing. After the market opened, HSBC's official exchange rates were announced, with both the British and American rates unchanged. Banks were actively swapping, resulting in busy but stable market conditions. Later, the silver balancing tax was announced to rise by half a cent. Banks traded shillings and swaps, with no significant changes in the end. By the time the market closed at noon, the selling price for the near-term British exchange rate was 1 shilling, 2.2 pence, 0.375 and 0.40625 pairing, and the US exchange rate was 30.1875 yuan, which was unchanged for the British and down 0.03125 for the US compared to the previous closing. Yesterday at the Chinese Securities Exchange, the dull market situation remained unchanged. The Chengdu incident is under investigation, and market sentiment seemed slightly affected. Bond prices hovered with slight weakness. Yesterday, at the opening, bond numbers 10 and 47 saw some short covering, and numbers 14 and 35 were offered, with supply and demand being very balanced. Although there were many transactions in 96 bond, there was still no upward movement. There were 600,000-700,000 yuan worth of purchases of number 70 bonds, immediately followed by 500,000-600,000 yuan worth of sales of number 11 bonds. Market conditions still failed to rise. The D bond was completely unable to open. After the market opened in the afternoon, there were some swap transactions, and market conditions still fluctuated between 0.05 and 0.1. At the closing, there were significant sales of number 53 bonds, and bonds E, C, and A fell by a small 0.1 to 0.15, with the rest unchanged. Market momentum seemed to be gradually triggering volatility, awaiting significant developments in the current situation. As a result, market prices, except for number 96 which rose slightly by 0.05 to 0.1, uniformly fell by a small 0.05 to 0.1 to 0.3. The total number of transactions was 3,405,000 yuan. The results of the rise and fall are compared and listed on the left (unit: yuan, transaction unit: 100 yuan):

Metals　White Lead Sheet Price Surge Resumes—Local Market Prices Also Increase by Several Dollars—

According to a cable received yesterday from foreign firms, the price of white lead sheet has risen to £18 per ton, a further increase of ten shillings compared to the previous price. Local operators, due to the high prices, are undecided, resulting in no transactions. However, the local market price has increased by several dollars due to the rising cost. For example, No. 2 is selling for 150-160 yuan (due to stock shortage), No. 3 is 140 yuan, Nos. 4 and 5 are 125 yuan, Nos. 6 and 7 are 120 yuan, and No. 8 and above are all selling for 122-123 yuan. Trading is still lively at the Gold Exchange.

Popular Lecture

Cotton Yarn: Rumor of Increased Import Taxes in Hebei and Chahar Causes Market Crash, Followed by Recovery Due to Profit-Taking

The yarn market experienced a morning drop followed by an afternoon recovery, but the trend was exceptionally volatile. This was because of divided opinions. Rumors spread that Hebei and Chahar were planning to impose new taxes on imported goods, causing sellers to become extremely active, especially foreign firms who rushed to sell off their holdings. In the afternoon, it was said that three firms profited handsomely and left the market, which was a good thing.

Price of Marked Yarn Still Drops by 50-60 Cents

In the early market for marked yarn, American cotton continued to rise, and the price of third-grade yarn also increased. Both bulls and bears were active in the market, resulting in inconsistent prices, with near-term contracts falling by 30-40 cents and far-term contracts rising by 20-70 cents. Unexpectedly, in the second session, the near-term decline moderated, while the far-term contracts fell by 1.37 yuan. Mingde, Hexing, Runkang, and Fukang engaged in heavy selling, while Hengyi, Gengfeng, Ruida, Senkang, and Xincheng actively covered their short positions. However, the overall situation remained weak, and as a result, prices for all months fell by 70-90 cents to 1.34 yuan compared to the previous day's closing price. The market atmosphere was quite weak at the opening of the afternoon session. Concerns about the Hebei and Chahar tariff issue led to unease, causing prices to decline steadily. Subsequently, large players took profits, causing the market to recover sharply. As a result, prices for all months rose by 40-60 cents to 1.10 yuan compared to the morning closing price. It was found that Xincheng sold 4,500 bales, Deda 1,200 bales, Tongji 1,600 bales, Juxing 1,400 bales, Jinchang 1,200 bales, Mingde 3,450 bales, Hexing 1,600 bales, Huamao 1,200 bales, Shenji 2,200 bales, Runkang 3,150 bales, Shengyuan 2,000 bales, and Jinkang 2,000 bales. Chengji bought 1,600 bales, Hengyi 3,000 bales, Yuda 2,450 bales, Dafeng 2,750 bales, Gengfeng 6,150 bales, Ruida 2,900 bales, and Senkang 3,500 bales. The highest and lowest prices of the day are listed on the left.

Spot Yarn Price Drops by One Yuan

Sales of spot yarn remained good. Today, various merchants purchased a total of 1,043 bales, with the price falling by one yuan. The purchase amounts for each merchant were as follows:

Nanjing 15 Guangdong 385 Inland 211

Ningbo 15 Tianjin 150 Changsha 210

Sichuan 75 Hankou 2

Cotton: Unstable Fluctuations

The cotton market remained weak, changing several times a day, but the overall trend did not deviate from a consolidation pattern. In reality, the harvest was abundant, and the market direction was not strong, coupled with foreign merchants selling off their holdings step by step, exerting significant pressure. However, in the afternoon session, short sellers took profits, causing prices to rise.

Marked Cotton Also Experiences Short Covering

In the early market for marked cotton, American cotton continued to rise by 8-11 points, and Osaka third-grade cotton rose by 50-60 cents. Market sentiment was slightly firm, and the weather was hot and humid, with intermittent sunshine and clouds, so there was no significant hidden selling. Prices for all months rose by 10-20 cents. Unexpectedly, in the second session, Juxing, Tongfeng, Fengtai, Yichang, Runkang, and Fukang uniformly offered to sell, and sellers took the opportunity to exert downward pressure, causing the decline to accelerate. The October contract broke through the seven-yuan level. The market recovered slightly in the third session, and the closing price returned to the same level. Changhe, Dafu, Yuda, Gengfeng, Yuanyi, and Yuanxingchang covered their short positions extensively. As a result, prices for all months fell by 0.05-1.30 yuan compared to the previous day's closing price. At the opening of the afternoon session, the market appeared ordinary and weak. Subsequently, short covering led to a price increase, resulting in prices for all contracts rising by 0.15-0.20 yuan compared to the morning closing price. Yuda sold 10,000 dan, Changfeng 2,600 dan, Daji 1,200 dan, Dafeng 2,000 dan, Hengyi 2,600 dan, Juxing 9,800 dan, Tongfeng 3,500 dan, Fengtai 5,000 dan, Shenji 2,700 dan, and Yichang 4,400 dan. Changhe bought 11,700 dan, Dachang 4,400 dan, Yuanxingchang 2,700 dan, Yuanyi 5,000 dan, Gengfeng 8,100 dan, Dafeng 4,500 dan, and Tongji 2,800 dan. Piece Goods: Japanese Merchants Dumping White Goods, Dye Factories Buying the Most Fine Twills – Chinese Factories' Light and Heavy Weight Coarse Cloth Also Slacken –

Dealers, in view of the tendency of Japanese merchants to dump white goods, including Longtou, Yanghe, Jixiang, Flower and Bird brands, and fine cloth, Blue Double Fish, Yanghe, Baobei brands, fine twills were secretly reduced in price. The local dye factories, because the autumn color cloth and color twills were still strong, occasionally bought spot white goods at cheap prices. Yesterday, various dye factories bought 300 pieces of various goods, with fine twills the most. The decline of fine cloth and fine twills from local factories was slower, still falling by 5-10 cents per piece yesterday. The 15.5-pound San Yuan Bao and 10-pound Jumping Child coarse cloth from the Japanese Shanghai factory, and the light and heavy weight coarse cloth from Chinese merchants such as Dasheng, Qingfeng, and Shenxin factories, also became more slack, falling by 9 cents per piece. Sales to customers were stagnant, and due to the raw cotton situation, everyone was wary. However, delivery of orders to various merchants was still busy, with inland and Yangtze replenishing sporadically, while the Fujian, Guangdong, Guizhou, and Yunnan areas gradually became active, replenishing mainly local factory fine cloth, fine twills, Zhigong, Serge, Flannel, and Printed Velvet goods, totaling 500 pieces. The Henan, Shaanxi, Northwest Road, and Shandong provinces still had a strong demand for Flannel, Printed Zhigong, and Serge.

Grains: Rumors of Japanese Merchants Buying Flour, Futures Flour and Wheat Rise Sharply in the Afternoon – Flour Up 4 Cents… Wheat Jumps 10 Cents

Flour: After the opening of the flour market in the morning, the market for each month presented a sharp rise after a fall, with foreign wheat quotations continuing to fall by one or two cents each. At the time of opening, the opening price broke through the one-cent mark, as low as 3.08 yuan, and futures months also fell by one or two cents. By the close, due to short covering, there was a slight rebound. When the afternoon session opened, it was flat at first, and later, non-professionals competed to cover short positions, and rumors spread that they would abandon wheat and buy flour, causing people to panic again, and buying increased greatly, and the months rose sharply, rising by two, three, or four cents more than the previous day. Such rumors are certainly unbelievable, but most of the rise was mainly due to short covering.

Wheat: The opening of the wheat market in the morning presented a rise after a flat start, with foreign wheat quotations down slightly by one or two cents, so the opening price for September and October continued to fall by two or three cents, and transactions below November were clear, and the debt was slightly stable. When the afternoon session opened, it was still stable at first, and later, the high price of the flour market boosted it greatly, causing the flour prices for each month after the first session to jump greatly. The reason for the rise was nothing more than the rumor of Japanese merchants buying flour, which caused excitement, and from six, seven, or eight cents higher than the previous day's closing price, it rose to as much as one dime. If the follow-up is not true, it is bound to rebound. The current wheat market is no longer rejected by factory customers, and they are selectively buying high-quality wheat, with Lin Huai Guan Ming Guang wheat at 4.95 yuan, second-grade at 4.9 yuan, Southern Suzhou wheat at 4.5 yuan, Bengbu wheat at 4.85 yuan, second-grade at 4.83 yuan, Jiangbei wheat at 4.77 yuan, Wuhu wheat at 4.72 yuan, and Huangqiao wheat at 4.78 yuan, with various factories such as Bufeng and Shenda buying more than 3,000 bags.
