Wu Xun, the Beggar Who Founded Schools

— Han Depu

"Eating well is not enough, building a charity school is what counts! Don't laugh at me for begging, just watch me build a charity school!"

During the Daoguang reign of the Qing Dynasty, an extraordinary person emerged in Tangyi County, Shandong. This person had a very peculiar temperament, not caring about food or clothing, but with a special love for establishing charity schools, specifically for accepting children from poor families to study—without charging a single penny. He established a total of three such charity schools. One might assume he was a wealthy scholar, but in fact, the opposite was true. He was not only illiterate but also a poor beggar. Perhaps you are skeptical? How could an illiterate beggar establish several charity schools? Isn't that strange? Indeed! Precisely because it is strange, it is worth recounting here.

This remarkable person's surname was Wu, given name Xun, the seventh child, living in Wujia Village, Tangyi County, where generations had farmed for a living. By Wu Xun's time, several consecutive years of famine meant the meager harvest couldn't feed the family. The family gradually declined. Wu Xun was already an adult, and seeing the situation was unsustainable, besides his elder brother and sister-in-law who went out to make a living, there was also a widowed mother in her fifties or sixties. It was a case of being under another's roof, and one could only lower one's head. In this situation, one could only brazenly take a broken basket, a broken bowl, and a dog-beating stick to beg for food.

Although Wu Xun begged for a living, he was very kind. He went out to beg for food every day, regardless of wind or rain. He would bring back any decent leftovers for his mother, and only eat what remained himself. The locals knew this and praised him as a filial beggar. After two years, Wu Xun's mother died of an old ailment, leaving Wu Xun alone. He then asked someone to introduce him to a scholarly family to work as a servant.

Although this family claimed to be from a family of scholars, the master was an exceptionally stingy pedant. His belly was full of poetry and the sayings of Confucius, his books never leaving his hand, giving the impression of importance, but in reality, he was a terrible person, constantly scheming against others. Wu Xun's employment in this family was truly unlucky.

One day, Wu Xun's sister asked someone to bring a letter and two strings of coins. It happened that Wu Xun had gone to the river to fetch water. The messenger thought it safest to hand them to the master to pass on to Wu Xun, and then left. Unexpectedly, the pedant saw the two strings of shiny coins and became envious. His mind twisted, and he planned to pocket them all. After all, Wu Xun was illiterate, how would he know?

When Wu Xun returned, the pedant said with a beaming smile, "Wu Qi, your sister has sent a letter to greet you! I'll read it to you." The letter was read, but not a word was mentioned about the two strings of coins.

By sheer coincidence, some time later, Wu Xun's relative happened to pass by and visited Wu Xun. He casually mentioned the aunt sending money through someone. Wu Xun said, "Good heavens! The master gave me the letter that day, but didn't mention any money!" Wu Xun's relative said, "He must have swallowed it! Go find him!" Hearing this, Wu Xun rushed back in a rage.

When Wu Xun saw the pedant, he was speechless. After a long pause, he stammered, "You…you…you swallowed the two strings of coins my sister sent. That won't do!" The pedant was engrossed in reading a copy of The Analects, but was suddenly stunned by Wu Xun's saying "swallowed," his eyes rolled upwards, and he slammed the table: "Preposterous! Who saw your sister send money?" With that, his nostrils flared, as if he were about to devour someone. Wu Xun took two steps back, helpless because he couldn't read, and the master had connections and influence. He could only suffer in silence, secretly shedding tears.

Time flew by, and it was almost New Year. The pedant, as usual, prepared for the holiday, writing some diamond-shaped Spring Festival couplets and ordering Wu Xun to paste them up, while he went to town to buy New Year goods. After the pedant left, a sudden gust of wind blew the couplets into a pile. Wu Xun was illiterate, so he randomly pasted them up. When the pedant returned in the evening and entered the house, he was furious and summoned Wu Xun, slapping him twice, scolding, "Are you blind? How did you paste these!" It turned out that Wu Xun had pasted "Cats and Dogs Peaceful" on the bed of the pedant and his wife, and "Family Auspiciousness" on the chicken coop. The couplets on the front and back doors had two upper lines on one side and two lower lines on the other. The rest were upside down or wrongly placed. Misplacing Spring Festival couplets was most taboo in ordinary households. The pedant's anger was no small matter. He immediately settled accounts and told Wu Xun to get out. The pedant worked the abacus and said, "Including wages and tea money, I'll deduct 20% to offset today's bad luck, leaving you with five hundred copper coins!" Wu Xun thought, "Anyway, I'm being kicked out. These few stinky coins won't make me any poorer." He raised his head and pointed at the pedant, scolding, "You swallowed my money and still want to deduct my wages. Do you have a conscience? I think these two stinky coins are dirty. Keep them to block the dog hole!" With a clatter, the coins were scattered all over the ground. Wu Xun grabbed his bundle, and without looking back, walked out, and from then on, he began his vagrant life.

After Wu Xun left the pedant's house, he thought: In the past, I suffered all kinds of hardships and was bullied because I was stupid, and I was stupid because I had no knowledge. Otherwise, my money wouldn't have been swallowed, and my wages wouldn't have been taken without payment. At the same time, he also thought: How many people in the world are as poor as I am and have no chance to study! Why don't I think of a way to establish a charity school to teach them to read, so they don't get cheated? But I'm a pauper, where would I get the money to run a school? He thought and thought, and decided to use his strength to do odd jobs for people, save the money he earned, and a charity school could definitely be established successfully. With that decided, he began to twist hemp threads every day, settling in a broken temple, going out to beg for food during the day, and saving every penny he got. He also composed many songs, singing to everyone he met: "Hired hands are bullied, better to beg for myself; don't look down on me for begging, sooner or later I'll build a charity school." People saw his awkward face, acting like a madman, begging everywhere, everyone thought he was crazy and ignored him, but he wasn't angry? He still sang in his mouth: "If you don't give me, I won't resent; good people will take care of my food."

Sometimes, when he went to beg for food and was scolded, he sang: "Grandpa and uncle, don't be angry, when you are not angry, I will leave." "Don't force, don't strengthen, don't be afraid! I beg for alms, you do good deeds, let's build a charity school together."

In the former Qing Dynasty, people all had queues behind their heads, but Wu Xun didn't have the time to put into braiding his queue. He shaved his head bald, leaving only a peach-shaped tuft of hair. When people laughed at him, he sang the following song for them to listen to: "Shave the left, leave the right, build a charity school, no need to worry."

After a few years, Wu Xun had saved ninety strings of coins, plus inherited two mu of ancestral land, which sold for one hundred and twenty strings of coins. Combined, he had two hundred and ten strings. He thought: To build a charity school, this money is far from enough! Keeping it on me isn't very safe, better to deposit it with Jinshi Lou. Master Lou is a sincere gentleman, in the future, the principal will generate interest, the interest will become principal, and the principal will generate more interest. If this continues, after a certain time, won't it be considerable? Thinking this, he sang casually: "Building a charity school, no worries, already have two hundred and ten strings." "Deposit the principal, generate interest, begging Jinshi Lou of Guantao (place name)."

Singing, he unknowingly arrived at Jinshi Lou's door. He knelt on both knees on the threshold and sang, "Don't want rice, don't want noodles, just beg to see Master Jinshi." The Lou family saw a mad beggar and waved him away, but Wu Xun knelt on the ground and wouldn't move, no matter how they drove him away, he refused to get up, continuing to sing: "Just beg to see Master Jinshi!" "Just beg to see Master Jinshi!"

The people around him found him both funny and pitiful, and gave him some food, vegetables and copper coins, but he didn't want them, insisting on making a scene until Jinshi Lou came out in person. He sang: "I beg for food, you do good deeds, take a look at the charity school I'm building." Jinshi Lou was confused and asked what he meant. He said, "I have two hundred and ten strings of coins, I want to deposit them in your house to earn interest, to be used for running a charity school." Jinshi Lou saw that he had such a good heart and agreed. He then sent two servants to fetch the two hundred and ten strings of coins and kept them for safekeeping to earn interest. From then on, Wu Xun deposited all the money he begged back with Jinshi Lou.

Sometimes people gave him better food, but he couldn't bear to eat it himself, and sold it to poor families, while he drank pot-washing water. When someone laughed at him, he sang: "Eating well is not enough, building a charity school is what counts." "Eating vegetable roots, eating vegetable roots, I don't need anyone for my meals; saving food, building a charity school." "Eating taro stems, eating taro stems, don't need fire, don't need water, saving money, building a charity school isn't difficult." The vegetable roots and taro stems in the garbage heap became his food.

His stomach was truly strange. If he couldn't beg for food or find vegetable roots and taro stems, he could fill his stomach with snakes, scorpions, broken bricks, and broken tiles. For him, it was a path to wealth. As long as you gave him money, he would eat them for you to see, and sing to you to relieve boredom: "Eating scorpions, eating scorpions, building a charity school is my business." "Snakes can be eaten, don't be afraid! Building a charity school is all my family's business." "Broken bricks and tiles, all can be digested; if I don't build a charity school, I'll be a laughingstock."

He also had a skill—standing a dragonfly, feet up, able to stand like that for half an hour without falling. When playing this game, he didn't need gongs or drums, he had his old tune: "Stand one, one coin, stand ten, ten coins; stand a lot, more money, who says I can't build a charity school?" As long as he was given enough money, he could crawl while standing, crawling and singing: "Crawl once, one string of coins, crawl ten times, ten strings of coins; building a charity school isn't difficult."

As the saying goes: "Nothing is difficult in the world, only those who don't put their heart into it," Wu Xun was exactly such a person. Day after day, he saved up seven or eight thousand strings of coins. Seeing that the amount was sufficient, he went to discuss it with Jinshi Lou. As a result, he bought more than two hundred mu of land, rented it out to people to cultivate, as a constant annual expense for the future charity school. The following year, by chance, a philanthropist named Guo was willing to donate two mu of good fields as the foundation for the charity school. So Jinshi Lou came forward and used Wu Xun's money to build more than twenty tiled houses, named "Chongxian Charity School," enrolling dozens of poor children. To invite Cui Juren to be the teacher, he knelt and begged for several days, finally touching Cui Juren's heart, and he agreed. In this way, Wu Xun's wish was finally fulfilled.

Although Wu Xun himself was illiterate, he was very serious about the students' studies. One day, while begging for money, he passed by the charity school and took a look inside. Unexpectedly, if he hadn't looked, it would have been fine, but when he looked, he was stunned. Why? It turned out that the young students, taking advantage of the teacher's nap, had sneaked off to enjoy themselves under the shade of the trees. Some were doing somersaults, some were grabbing each other's braids and fighting. Wu Xun watched through the cracks in the door for a long time, seeing no one to stop them, and couldn't help singing: "Studying without effort, no face to see parents; studying without heart, no face to see mother!" Hearing Wu Xun's voice, the students all rushed back to their seats.

Wu Xun walked into the classroom, but the teacher was not there. Looking into the bedroom, Teacher Cui was snoring loudly. He silently knelt down on both knees on the ground.

After a while, Teacher Cui woke up, and suddenly seeing Wu Xun kneeling upright, he was very ashamed and hurried to help Wu Xun up, saying: "Mr. Wu, why do you do this? I really feel bad about it. If there is anything wrong in the future, please tell me directly." Wu Xun sang nonchalantly: "Teacher sleeping, students messing around, I come to kneel, once and for all." Cui Juren's face turned red and apologized, saying: "From now on, I will definitely be diligent and dedicated." If students didn't study hard, he would kneel in front of them and beg them. In this way, even the laziest teachers and the most mischievous students would not dare to put down their books and play again.

In addition to running the charity school himself, Wu Xun valued every penny, not daring to waste a single cent, but he was willing to help the poor who did well. He heard people say that there was a Zhang family daughter-in-law in the area who served her mother-in-law very filially. Once, hoping that her mother-in-law would recover from illness, she secretly cut a piece of her own flesh to make soup for her to drink. After Wu Xun knew about this, he immediately gave her ten mu of good fields, and sang to people: "This person is good, this person is good, I give her ten mu and still feel it's not enough; this person is filial, this person is filial, give her ten mu to support her old age." On the contrary, he was not willing to help his lazy elder brother at all. He said: "My business, don't interfere, brothers live separately." He never changed his mind because of his brother.

One day, he walked in front of a large temple. The halls inside were very grand. He thought: Leaving such a good place unused to run a charity school, but worshiping these ghostly clay statues, isn't that foolish? He knocked on the door twice: "Temple big, monks many, why not build a charity school?" This caused a group of monks to laugh. Probably they laughed too hard, and it disturbed the abbot inside, who came out to inquire. Wu Xun sang: "I beg for food, don't laugh, take a look at the charity school I'm building." The abbot asked:

"Are you Mr. Wu, the charity school enthusiast? I've heard of you for a long time! I've heard of you for a long time!" Wu Xun quickly said, "I dare not! I dare not!" and followed the monk to the reception room.

This abbot had long heard of Wu Xun, and now that they met in person, he wouldn't miss the opportunity. He told Wu Xun to move to the Buddhist temple in the future, so that it would be convenient to come and go and rest. Wu Xun readily agreed. He lived in the temple for more than a year. The abbot donated all his savings of more than two thousand strings of coins to Wu Xun to run the charity school. Truly, sincerity moves everything.

His singing was very effective. Many people were moved by him, some giving money, some giving food and vegetables. He tied the money together with rope, sold the food and vegetables to others, and tied the money he sold them for together, counted the numbers, and sent them to Jinshi Lou's house, and then returned to the broken temple to be a partner with the clay Bodhisattva. He could adapt to please people. Once, he came out of the broken temple and just reached the temple gate when a broken tile from the corner of the roof fell and hit him on the head, and blood flowed straight down. He didn't care and covered the wound with a pinch of incense ash, and then he sang: "Breaking my head, venting the fire, building a charity school is all on me." The listeners almost laughed until their backs hurt. At daybreak, he left the broken temple and went out to beg for food again.

He had many ways to make money. Whenever he had free time, he would help people do odd jobs, regardless of sweeping manure, hoeing grass, or pushing the mill. Others worked for a fixed time, but he kept working until dark before stopping. He often sang like this: "Removing manure, hoeing grass, pushing the mill, come find me, no matter how dark, no matter how much money." "Pushing the mill, pushing the mill, sixty he for a dou of wheat, no matter the grinding or the sifting, money for sifting is even more." He usually held the attitude that he would laugh and scold at others, as long as you give money, he was willing to be spat on the face: "Charity school enthusiast, no temper, greets people with courtesy; money in hand, life is alive, building a charity school will last for ten thousand years."

Wu Xun's fame for begging for food and building schools spread day by day. Almost everyone in Shandong province knew about it. Later, even the governor knew about it and busily sent someone to summon him. Sure enough, his reputation was well-deserved, crazy and crazy: "I'm not crazy, I'm not sick, I only have a charity school disease." He kept singing. When the governor visited the charity school, the results were not bad, so he prepared a memorial to request the court to commend him.

One day, Wu Xun was begging for food outside when he suddenly saw an official sedan chair approaching from afar. He thought that there must be a great official sitting in the sedan chair. Not to be missed, he threw down his broken bowl and dog-beating stick, and knelt down on both knees on the ground. He opened his throat to sing.

Seeing someone kneeling in front of him, the sedan chair carrier thought it was someone filing a lawsuit and shouted, "Listen, kneeling on the ground, Vice Minister Yu is here. If you have a grievance or a lawsuit, you can tell the truth!" Wu Xun sang: "No lawsuit, no complaint, building a charity school is what I'm good at, great lord, donate some money to help!" Vice Minister Yu thought: This person is very strange, could he be the charity school enthusiast Wu Xun? He asked, "Are you Wu Qi?" Wu Xun said, "I am." Vice Minister Yu said, "Good! I will donate to the charity school soon." Wu Xun crawled on the ground and kowtowed, happily walking away.

After some time, he suddenly received an imperial decree, conferring Wu Xun as "Charity School Administrator," bestowing a yellow jacket, and awarding a plaque with "Loves to Do Good" written on it, to be hung in the charity school, what glory! But Wu Xun didn't find it strange at all. He sang casually: "Charity school enthusiast, no need to be conferred! Yellow jacket, no use! Building a charity school will last for ten thousand years." He still lived his begging life.

Someone advised him to marry a wife, so that he could have descendants in the future, but he always shook his head: "Don't marry a wife, don't have children, building a charity school is selfless." Until his death, he remained a bachelor. He often used this song to express his ambition: "Life is rare at seventy, fifty-three years old and not married, relatives and friends are all dead, in the end, only the charity school disease." He also saw the issue of life and death very calmly. He sang: "Die on the road, bury on the road, die in the street, bury in the street, there will naturally be a coffin when you die."

He died in the twenty-second year of Guangxu—he lived to be fifty-nine years old. His entire estate was these three charity schools he founded, and nothing else. On the day of his funeral, there were more than 10,000 people to see him off, many of whom were students from the charity school. All of them were crying bitterly, lamenting and praising him! His bones were buried next to the charity school. Even now, those broken baskets and broken bowls—his relics, and the charity school he founded, are still well preserved in Linqing County, Shandong!

Otto Bismarck

— Yun Bo

Bismarck was the hero who created Germany. Although some say he advocated autocracy, promoted militarism, and was a troublemaker, his perseverance and planning are worthy of our admiration; his achievements and aspirations are worthy of our respect.

In the past, when Germany was not yet unified, there were many small states of the German nation, which organized a federal government. This federal government was dominated by Austria, but Austria was not of the same ethnicity as them.

Among these many federations, there was a larger kingdom called Prussia. Bismarck was a Prussian. He was born into the aristocracy, and in his youth, he was very dissolute, disregarding etiquette, fond of drinking, and often engaged in duels; sometimes he practiced shooting, and the booming of gunfire never stopped all day long; his neighbors all hated him and called him "Riotous Young Master." But after his father died, he was sad day and night, not showing any signs of wildness. This shows that he had passionate feelings and a sincere personality; he was truly a heroic figure.

When he was studying at school, he liked to study history and geography very much. When he read history and talked about the situation in which France had ravaged Prussia in the past, he wanted to avenge himself. He saw in history that any country with a mixed race would eventually split up, so he wanted to exclude Austria and let Prussia lead this German federation of the same race. He saw geographically that any country with a system of construction would eventually dissolve, so he wanted to unify the various federations and create a united and strong country. These few points of view were the goals of his lifelong efforts.

He paid close attention to the international situation. When he traveled to England and France, he often paid attention to examining the politics of various countries and studied them very carefully. He even carefully explored the temperament of the French Emperor. He saw the corruption of Austrian politics and the mediocrity of its ministers, and he was confident that his aspirations would definitely be successful. When he was the envoy to Russia, he felt that among the European countries, only Russia could be an assistant, and his foreign policy was to contact Russia in everything. He had very precise preparations for his life's work.

At that time, King William I of Prussia was thinking of unifying the federation and making Prussia the leader of the federation. He prepared to reform the military system, expand military preparations, and actively increase military strength. However, the parliament did not approve of this move and vehemently opposed it. The King of Prussia felt that there was no way, so he appointed Bismarck as Prime Minister to confront the parliament.

Because Bismarck was a descendant of the aristocracy, he had an arrogant personality and developed the idea of autocracy and reverence for the king. He believed that in Prussia at that time, only by acting arbitrarily could he freely use his means to achieve the goal of unifying the federation, and the parliament and constitution were enough to hinder his policy of advancing bravely. After he became Prime Minister, he dismissed all the civil and military officials who opposed the reform of the military system; and decided to dissolve the parliament. Everything the government wanted to do, such as expanding military preparations, reforming the military system, and increasing military spending, was immediately implemented. He said to the representatives of the people: "At present, various problems can only be solved with iron and blood." From then on, everyone called him the "Iron and Blood Chancellor."

At this time, the people of the whole country hated him because he excluded civil rights, dismissed the parliament, and prohibited freedom of speech and publication, and regarded him as an enemy. However, Bismarck had a broad vision and a firm ambition, and he did not care about the opposition of the people, but only tried his best to implement his plans. He believed that in that scattered situation, nothing could be accomplished without being strong and capable; he also believed that his actions were beneficial to the German nation and not for his own self-interest. In the future, when he succeeded, the people would always understand him. Therefore, with the spirit of sacrificing himself for the country, he tried his best to do the great cause of unifying the federation.

Although some people wanted to assassinate him, he was still not afraid. He said: "To make the people happy, just hang me. But I still want to unify Germany and make Germany rich and strong, so I can't die yet. After a few more years, when my policy is successful, the people will definitely welcome me!"

The first time he implemented the "Iron and Blood Policy" was to go to war with Denmark. He deliberately made an alliance with Austria, so that Austria could not unite with other countries, and he could also use this to test Austria's military strength. How far-reaching his intentions were!

When Prussia defeated Denmark and signed a treaty with Austria, it deliberately competed with Austria for rights, arousing Austria's anger. As a result, it went to war with Austria and easily defeated Austria. The goal of excluding Austria was achieved.

Prussia won two consecutive victories, and its national power gradually became stronger. This made the French Emperor very jealous, and finally he went to war with France again. In the war, he used swift means to capture the French capital, Paris. William I was crowned emperor of the German Federation in Paris. All the federations were afraid of Prussia's power and expressed their willingness to obey the command of the Prussian Emperor. Bismarck's ambition of unification, which he had accumulated for several years, was finally successful.

Although Bismarck advocated the Iron and Blood Policy, his policy changed after the unification of Germany. He had previously advocated dictatorship, but now he followed the trend of the world and advocated national socialism; respected freedom, valued civil rights, established a constitution, opened a parliament, revised the new criminal law, promoted free trade, and worked hard to improve industry. He worked hard to do construction work to consolidate the foundation of the country. Under his guidance, Germany gradually became prosperous and became a strong country in Europe.

Bismarck had a majestic appearance, a vibrant spirit, a strong physique, worked diligently, was very willing to take responsibility, and had a firm will, dared to act and dared to do, and was not afraid of difficulties and all obstacles. His perseverance is very admirable. Although he was so decisive, he planned very carefully beforehand. When he encountered something, he must first carefully examine its appearance, and then carefully examine its results. If there is danger, he must carefully measure the size of the danger and calculate how to prevent that danger. He would never do anything inappropriate, and the policies he implemented never failed.

He did not like war, because war is always dangerous. After the unification of Germany, he never used the "Iron and Blood Policy." Whenever the friendship between the two countries could be maintained with difficulty and there was no need to use force, he would never easily go to war with others. The several battles he fought were all unavoidable, and they were decided only after decades of calm consideration. He once said: "We cannot see the cards that God is playing." Although he was very confident of winning, he was still often afraid of failure. If we say that he is rude and dissolute, and likes to be ambitious and greedy for success, then we have misunderstood his personality.

Later, Bismarck resigned and retired because of disagreements with the new emperor, William II. At that time, he was already seventy-five years old. When he was sitting alone in a carriage and was about to leave the German capital, Berlin, many people on the side of the road presented him with flower wreaths. The sound of praise and blessings was like thunder. Bismarck got out of the car at that time and said goodbye to them. The people surrounded him and cheered. Bismarck was moved to tears, and the people also sadly wept and saw him off. What Bismarck had said before was indeed fulfilled. How much the people love him now!

Publishing World

Jane Eyre's Autobiography (3)

— Chen Youqin

Written by Ms. C. Bronte of England, translated by Li Jiye, published by the Life Bookstore World Literature Series

Jane Eyre's talents are multifaceted (she is good at painting, especially talkative, which made her master secretly fall in love with her). Her personality is extremely rebellious and has a firm sense of autonomy. Rochester is more than twice Jane Eyre's age and is not a very handsome man (although Jane Eyre herself is not considered beautiful). The classes of the two are also very far apart, and there is no possibility of love between them. However, after a long time of confiding in each other, Jane Eyre's small and pure heart was secretly engraved with a small shadow of the strong and eccentric male Rochester.

One night, when Jane Eyre had not yet fallen asleep, she heard footsteps, secretly got up to track them, and found someone setting a fire to burn Rochester to death. She secretly saved him again. Rochester told her not to publicize it, and he left the next day. Soon after, he brought many distinguished guests (including many noble ladies and beautiful young ladies) and lingered in Thornfield for a long time. There was once a rumor that Rochester was going to marry the aristocratic Miss Ingram.

Miss Ingram lived in Thornfield Manor for a long time, and they played many of the pastimes that nobles often play, such as singing, hunting, dancing, and playing cards, etc. Of course, Jane Eyre was not included in these, because Jane Eyre was just a humble nanny. Miss Ingram often showed a contemptuous attitude towards Jane Eyre and Adela, and became more and more intimate with Rochester day by day.

Rochester was really strange. He suddenly disguised himself as an old witch and began to tell fortunes for all the nobles and even the people living in his mansion. No one knew that he was Rochester, because a few days ago he had announced that he was going out to prepare for the wedding. Finally, he told Jane Eyre's fortune and revealed his true form.

Later, the two of them secretly did something to save his friend Mason from being bitten and stabbed by a madman, and the two of them became more spiritually compatible.

Miss Ingram was willing to marry Rochester only to get half of his property. Later, there was a rumor that he did not have much property and was in debt, so the marriage contract was broken. Rochester once said this to Jane Eyre:

"I pretended to court Miss Ingram because I wanted you to love me as crazily as I love you; and I knew that to promote this purpose, jealousy was the best ally I could ask for." - Page 241

The wedding proceeded smoothly. When Rochester and Jane Eyre announced their marriage, everyone was very surprised and thought that this combination was extremely inappropriate. Sure enough, good things take time. When a pastor was invited to take the oath in the cathedral, several people who disrupted the wedding suddenly appeared from the guests who were watching the ceremony. One was the lawyer Brookley, who was asked by Jane Eyre's uncle, Mr. Eyre, to come out to stop this false marriage; the other was Mason, who had been bitten and stabbed by a madman in Thornfield. The reason they stopped was that Rochester had already been married, and the bride was Mason's sister. And it was proved that Rochester's wife was still alive and still in Thornfield Manor.

Talk

Guangdong Province Implements Anti-Gambling and Anti-Smoking Policies

— Fang

The biggest evils in Guangdong Province are smoking and gambling, and the people suffer the most from them. When Chen Jitang left, his private property totaled several tens of millions of Hong Kong dollars in cash, several tens of millions of dollars in assets, and real estate worth no less than several tens of millions of dollars. The total amount Chen Jitang had amassed in Guangdong over the years was almost incalculable. Although this wealth may not have been entirely derived from smoking and gambling, a large portion of it certainly was.

What did the people of Guangdong do to deserve this torment? They were ruined and impoverished, becoming as thin and gaunt as jackals. Although everyone knows the harm of smoking and gambling, the people of Guangdong themselves do not know how to cherish themselves and willingly throw themselves into the net, reaping what they sow, so what else is there to say? The love of good things is inherent in everyone, and the enjoyment of comfort is sweet to all. If the government uses this to tempt people, how can people restrain themselves? As a result, every drop of the local people's lifeblood flows into Chen's pocket.

Addiction to smoking and gambling leads to the abandonment of everything else, leaving one bedridden, turning day into night, shouting and gambling, emptying coffers and baskets, and then regretting it, but it is already too late. Therefore, the harm of smoking and gambling is that, in small terms, it is enough to ruin families and lives, and in large terms, it is enough to destroy countries and extinguish races. Consider what kind of country our nation is in now, and what kind of countries other nations are in now. Countries like Germany and Italy promote eugenics, and people who are disabled, weak, or ill are not only forbidden to marry but are also sterilized. Why? Because in the current world of survival of the fittest, there is no room for the disabled, weak, or ill among the people.

Now, if ordinary outstanding and promising citizens of our country become addicted to bad habits, they become like useless people. If they are immersed in gambling, they ignore everything else. What benefit do such people bring to the country? They cause the nation to become increasingly degenerate. If a nation in this state wants to resist the great powers, it will only be eliminated and trampled upon. Therefore, after our central government unified Guangdong Province, it first banned smoking and gambling to eliminate the great evils of the people of Guangdong and to strengthen the country, which is why the people of Guangdong are raising their hands, shedding tears, and celebrating endlessly.

According to recent news from Hong Kong, Guangdong will implement a ban on gambling on September 1st. All legitimate and illegal gambling dens in the province will close by the 31st night, resulting in the unemployment of over 100,000 people. Smoking will be banned in 29 years, and drugs will be banned in 25 years. The reason why smoking and gambling are so prevalent in Guangdong Province is simply because those at the top advocate it, and those at the bottom readily follow. If this continues for a few more years, the chances of the people of Guangdong not having all their property taken by Chen alone will be slim. Therefore, Chen's presence was the misfortune of the people of Guangdong, and Chen's inability to maintain his position for long and his forced departure now is the great fortune of the people of Guangdong.

The implementation of the ban on gambling has resulted in the unemployment of as many as 100,000 people, which seems to be a cause for concern for these people. However, those who rely solely on gambling for a living are generally loafers and idlers, and bandits and rogues with no regular occupations. They originally relied on gambling because they were unemployed, and they are definitely not unemployed because of gambling. These gamblers are originally figures from vocational training centers for vagrants, and the result will only be to drive them into vocational training centers. There is no need to worry about them.

Correction: In the third paragraph of yesterday's "Talk," the three words "still not" were omitted after "and it is killing humanely."

At the Ancient City Wall

— Xia Ying

Facing the scenery of this ancient city, he began to exclaim. "This lovely, quiet southern city!" he murmured. I watched his expression; this time, I even discovered his poetic emotions. Isn't it a strange thing? Such a gentle and polite young man fighting to the death in the artillery fire! I couldn't help but ask him why he joined the army; and his thoughts on the battlefield. After hearing my questions, he laughed, reached out and patted my shoulder, and said:

"How can I answer your questions? You are too young now, you won't understand. I can only tell you that I joined the army for a living! A person always has to find a bowl of rice to eat; isn't going to war the same principle? Although, when the country really needs me, when I have to resist foreign powers, then I am fulfilling a citizen's duty! On the battlefield, I feel that if one day the muzzles of our millions of brothers are aimed outwards, then even if I am crushed to pieces, it is what I desire! But now, every time I go to the battlefield, I feel an unspeakable pain..."

"Yes, Company Commander Fang, if the muzzles are aimed outwards, I would be willing to go to war with you," I said excitedly.

"Really? That's great!" he said excitedly, and patted my back again. "You are still young, study hard, and there will always be a chance for you to participate in resisting foreign powers... Listen, that pockmarked bugler is blowing the assembly call again, let's go back."

A series of chaotic bugle calls sounded, and we got up and walked down the city wall.

Company Commander Fang was transferred not long after. Our parting did not involve any sorrow or attachment, but he did reveal a kind of indescribable melancholy for this ancient city, as if he was infinitely regretful. Autumn was already deep, and the wind was very cold. I just repeatedly told him to take care...

This was my impression of the seventh autumn – the last autumn – in that ancient city. On a day when a fierce north wind was blowing, and the sky was gray and cold, I said goodbye to my home and embarked on my long journey. One year, two years, three years... The memory of the ancient city wall gradually faded away in the torrent of life. Now that another autumn has arrived, it truly evokes endless emotion.

Home

— Fang Zong

At night, as soon as it gets dark, there are unusually few pedestrians on the road. Only soldiers with bayonets hanging from their waists run and laugh in groups of two or three. Some are drunk, and some harass women on the road. In the desolate streets and alleys, only crisp footsteps sound heavily, and that heavy sound strikes people's hearts again and again. Few "Chinese" are seen, especially women.

I sat at home, chatting with an old neighbor. In front of the dim oil lamp, he—this businessman who was no longer young—excitedly, yet cautiously, lowered his voice and spoke to me.

"Why did you come back here?" His tone carried a hint of complaint.

"How can I not come back? This is my home. I want to see everything in my home!"

"Ah, home, do you still have a home? Can your home still live here? I advise you, you should quickly move your entire family to Guannei, Beiping, Tianjin—oh, no, I heard those places aren't good either. You should still move to the south, Shanghai, Guangdong!" He took a puff of smoke, "It's a pity I don't have money, and my store is closed. If I can raise enough for travel expenses, I will definitely move, move to Guannei..."

"Don't be sad. Slowly, we will always guard our home and drive out the ××s!" I comforted him, while encouraging him and myself in this way.

Slowly! Slowly until when? Until when will we guard? Don't you know that we Chinese are no longer having a good life here. They are taking everything's livelihood…
